# Changelog

All notable changes to findajob are documented in this file.

The format is based on [Keep a Changelog](https://keepachangelog.com/en/1.1.0/),
and this project adheres to [Semantic Versioning](https://semver.org/spec/v2.0.0.html).

Until the pipeline stabilizes, 0.x releases are considered unstable. Breaking
changes may land in minor version bumps; patch releases are bugfix-only.

## [Unreleased]

### Added

- **In-app "update available" banner** (#1016): the dashboard now shows a dismissible banner when a newer findajob release exists on GitHub — `vX → vY`, a CHANGELOG "what's new" link, and a per-substrate update hint (Fly → redeploy from the dashboard; Docker → `docker compose pull && up -d`, or Watchtower if you run it). The check compares the running CHANGELOG version against GitHub's `releases/latest` (anonymous, tuple-compared), caches in-memory ~daily, refreshes after the response so it never blocks page render, and fails open (no banner if the check can't resolve). Dismissal is version-keyed, so the next release re-surfaces it. No new env var; no schema change.

### Changed

- **Corrected the Fly auto-deploy update claim** (#1017): `install-fly.md` and `updating.md` no longer say enabling Fly's "Auto-Deploy on push" delivers automatic updates — it only redeploys when *the connected GitHub repo* is pushed, which a wild user's fork is not when this project releases upstream. The accurate path (dashboard **Deploy** / redeploy) is now primary. Docs-only.
- **Site-doc accuracy sweep — install / deploy / Gmail** (#1014): an audit of all user-facing site docs against the validated install path corrected stale or wrong info. `getting-started/README.md`: dropped the "from `fly auth login`" framing (install-fly.md is now no-terminal web) and fixed a broken `install-fly.md §7` anchor → §6. `operations/install-docker.md`: broken `api-keys.md` link (resolved to a nonexistent `operations/api-keys.md`) → `../getting-started/api-keys.md`. `operations/fly-deploy.md`: "all six volumes" → the single `findajob_state` volume (Fly = one volume/machine), and the DB-inspect path `/app/data/pipeline.db` → `/app/state/data/pipeline.db`. `updating.md`: the Fly section is reframed (web Auto-Deploy + dashboard redeploy for no-terminal installs, CLI as the power-user-with-clone path) and the stale "automated Fly updates planned for a future release" note (which contradicted install-fly.md) is removed. `troubleshooting.md`: Gmail was described as OAuth2 / device-flow pointing at a nonexistent `scripts/gmail_auth.py`; corrected to the real IMAP + Google app-password mechanism configured at `/config/gmail/`. Docs-only.
- **Fly install guides reflect the validated one-click flow** (#1012): `start-here-fly.md` and `install-fly.md` now tell you to accept the launch wizard's defaults (including the **Internal port**) — corrected from the prior claim that the repo `fly.toml` overrides the wizard's port, which it does not. The obsolete "Could not find image" 404 walkthrough (the bug fixed at the source by #1002/#1010) is trimmed to a brief retry safety-net. Docs-only.

### Fixed

- **No-CLI Fly web install now deploys healthy when you accept all defaults** (#1010): after #1002 made the web "Launch from GitHub" build + run, the deploy still failed its health check unless the user manually changed the launch wizard's Internal port to 8090 — Fly's wizard defaults the port to **8080** and ignores the repo `fly.toml`'s `internal_port` (and the Dockerfile `EXPOSE`, which the pre-build wizard can't read), while uvicorn served 8090. uvicorn's port is now env-driven (`FINDAJOB_INTERNAL_PORT`, default 8090) and the root `fly.toml` (the web-launch config) targets **8080** and sets `FINDAJOB_INTERNAL_PORT=8080` via `[env]` (which the wizard applies to the machine), so the wizard's 8080 default matches the app with no user action. `ops/fly.toml*` and compose are unchanged at 8090 — the CLI deploy path and every existing deploy keep serving 8090. **No `migration-required`** — the default port is unchanged; only the web-launch config differs.
- **`EXPOSE 8090` added to the Dockerfile** (#1008): documents the port uvicorn serves and helps the *CLI* `fly launch` port scan. It does **not** fix the web "Launch from GitHub" wizard — that wizard sets the port field before building the image, so it can't read `EXPOSE`; the web-launch port fix is #1010 above. Metadata-only — no runtime change; the CLI deploy path and compose were already correct.
- **Prep cost logging no longer under-counts on failed, truncated, or empty LLM calls** (#955): `run_role` (the prep/interview LLM wrapper) skipped the `cost_log` write on `OpenRouterError`, on null-content (`finish_reason=length`) truncations, and on empty output — but OpenRouter bills for consumed tokens in all three cases, so `spend_this_month()` under-counted exactly during failure/truncation storms, when spend is highest. `run_role` now writes a `cost_log` row on every terminating branch: a billed-but-empty success records its cost (the old `and text` guard silently dropped these), and a billed-but-failed `OpenRouterError` records its cost when OpenRouter returned usage — `OpenRouterError` now carries `cost_usd`/`prompt_tokens`, parsed at the null-content raise site alongside the existing `completion_tokens` (#737), so the failure row is fully API-authoritative. A pre-response failure that never billed (network/auth) still writes no row, so free failures don't inflate the total. The scoring path is unchanged. **No `migration-required`** — uses the existing `cost_log` columns.
- **A spend-ceiling breach (or fail-closed gate DB error) mid-prep no longer strands the job** (#956): the prep orchestrator's Phase A and Phase B handlers caught only `subprocess.CalledProcessError`, so a `LLMSpendCeilingExceeded` (deliberately not an `OpenRouterError`, so `run_role` re-raises it) — or a raw `sqlite3.OperationalError` propagated by the fail-closed ceiling gate when `pipeline.db` is unavailable — fell through uncaught, leaving the job in `prep_in_progress` for up to 60 minutes until the watchdog, with no notification. Both phases now catch these and recover immediately: Phase A resets to `scored`, Phase B resets to `briefing_ready` (preserving the briefing folder so the operator can retry Phase B without re-paying Phase A), each writing a `.failed_prep` sentinel and firing a `prep_failure` ntfy. Recovery is stage-guarded — a transient error surfacing *after* the success stage was already committed (e.g. on the post-commit audit write) does not revert a completed prep or fire a misleading failure ntfy. The contradictory comments that claimed the ceiling gate no-ops "when pipeline.db is unavailable" — in both `openrouter.complete()` and `spend_ceiling.py`'s module docstring — are corrected to match the gate's actual fail-closed contract (`spend_ceiling.check_call_gate` is authoritative — DB errors propagate; the orchestrator is the layer that recovers). The watchdog remains the backstop for genuine hangs. **No `migration-required`** — no schema change.

## [0.33.0] — 2026-06-03

### Added

- **Change your timezone after onboarding** (#988): a new `/settings/timezone/` page lets you pick a different IANA zone without re-running the onboarding interview. It shows the currently running `TZ` plus any picked-but-pending zone, validates the selection (`ZoneInfo`), and writes `data/timezone` atomically — invalid input is rejected inline with no partial write. The change takes effect on the next app restart (same semantics as the onboarding pick and the dashboard restart-to-apply banner, #981), and that banner now links straight here. A shared sub-nav (`templates/settings/_settings_nav.html`) cross-links every `/settings/` page so each is reachable from the others.
- **Onboarding suggests your timezone from your browser** (#989): a new timezone-confirmation step after the interview pre-selects your IANA zone from `Intl.DateTimeFormat().resolvedOptions().timeZone` and lets you accept or override it before continuing. The confirmed pick is written to `data/timezone` and supersedes the interviewer's location-to-zone conversion; when the browser value is unavailable (no JS, unresolvable zone), the step falls back to the interviewer-derived value so the LLM-conversion path is preserved. Both surfaces share a single validated, atomic `findajob.timeutil.write_timezone_file` helper. No schema change.

### Changed

- **`uv sync` now installs findajob itself** (#978): `pyproject.toml` gained a `[build-system]` table (setuptools backend), so `uv sync` installs the findajob package (editable) alongside its dependencies in one step. Fresh git worktrees and clean dev checkouts no longer need a separate `uv pip install -e .` before `import findajob` works. CI's install step collapses to `uv sync --locked --extra dev`, with lint/type/test now run via `uv run`. The Docker build commands are unchanged: `pip install --require-hashes` cannot hash an editable install, so findajob stays excluded from the hashed export (`--no-emit-project`) and is editable-installed separately (now resolving the explicit `setuptools.build_meta` backend rather than pip's legacy PEP 517 fallback — equivalent for this src-layout package). No runtime or operator-facing behavior change.
- **Outreach contact ranking is no longer hardcoded to one career field** (#964): the contact ranker (`find_contacts.rank_contacts`, which picks which of your LinkedIn connections at a company to draft outreach to) carried a hardcoded domain-vocabulary tier — data-center/infrastructure terms — that only boosted relevance for one field. Those terms now come from an optional gitignored `config/ranking_boost_terms.yaml` (with a field-agnostic `.yaml.example`), loaded via `config_loader.load_ranking_boost_terms()`; the executive, seniority, and recruiting tiers stay built in (they're field-neutral). A missing file means no domain boost, so the repo carries no field-specific vocabulary (per `docs/maintainers/generalization.md`). The file is editable via the `/config/` raw editor and hot-reloads on the next prep run. **To keep a domain boost, seed `config/ranking_boost_terms.yaml` with your field's terms** (see the `.example`). Folds in the dead-`network_depth`-column removal below.
- **Feedback analyzer's title-keyword signals are no longer hardcoded to one field** (#1004): `analyze_feedback`'s "applied vs rejected" keyword analysis carried a hardcoded data-center/infrastructure keyword list, plus a second field-locked exclusion list in the false-positive word-frequency section. The tracked keywords now come from a non-empty field-neutral default (`manager`, `engineer`, `senior`, `director`, `lead`, `program`) overridable via an optional gitignored `config/title_signal_keywords.yaml` (`config_loader.load_title_signal_keywords()`, with a field-agnostic `.yaml.example`); the false-positive word-frequency noise list drops the field-specific words (`data`, `center`, `operations`), keeping only generic + universal title-word noise. Unlike the #964 ranking boost, the default is **non-empty** so the section stays useful out of the box (mirrors `reject_reasons`). No data-driven redesign — section 8's n-gram recurrence analysis already covers corpus-adaptive discovery. Editable via `/config/`, hot-reloaded next run.

### Removed

- **`jobs.network_depth` column** and its last writer (the `network_depth=?` clause in the triage orchestrator's enrich UPDATE) — see *Migration required* below (#964). The sibling `known_contacts` column is retained.

### Fixed

- **Web "Launch an App from GitHub" deploy 404 (`Could not find image`)** (#1002): the recommended no-terminal Fly install (#881) failed deterministically — Fly's "Build image" step showed green, then "Deploy application" 404'd on `registry.fly.io/<app>:deployment-<sha>`. Root cause: the root `fly.toml` pinned a prebuilt `[build] image`, which Fly's Depot-based GitHub launcher does not reliably honor — the Depot build step is skipped (an image is "already specified"), so the deployment tag the deploy step references is never built, and the deploy 404s on it. The root `fly.toml` (the web-launch config) now builds the Dockerfile instead (`[build] dockerfile = "Dockerfile"`), so the image it deploys actually exists; web-launch deploys now run a ~few-minute image build. `ops/fly.toml` and `ops/fly.toml.example` are unchanged — the CLI path still pulls the prebuilt `ghcr.io/brockamer/findajob:latest` image (fast, no build). Resolves the root cause behind #999's documented fallback. **No `migration-required`** — existing stacks and the CLI deploy path are unaffected.
- **First-deploy "Could not find image" 404 on the Fly web path** (#999): a first-time installer following `docs/getting-started/start-here-fly.md` could hit a failed first deploy — Fly's "Build image" step goes green, then "Deploy application" fails with `failed to create release (status 404): … Could not find image …` — with no troubleshooting branch in the guide. The recommended no-terminal "Launch an App from GitHub" flow builds the repo's Dockerfile rather than reliably pulling the prebuilt `ghcr.io/brockamer/findajob` image named in `fly.toml`'s `[build] image`, and the build→registry handoff can 404. Both Fly guides (`start-here-fly.md`, `install-fly.md`) now carry a tiered fix: delete any stray launch-form Variable, retry the deploy (clears the transient registry race), then fall back to the CLI deploy path — which pulls the prebuilt image and never builds, so it can't hit this 404 class. The undocumented launch-form "Variables / Name-Value" field (which a user can mistake for the API-key entry) is also now called out as leave-blank. **No `migration-required`** — documentation only.
- **False "inside contact" signals on the board for short-named companies** (#963): the ingest-time contact matcher used substring containment, so a connection at "GreenApple" would light up the amber contact cell on an "Apple" job, and the two-letter company "AI" matched any connection whose company merely contained "ai" (e.g. "AIRBUS"). Ingest now routes through the same canonical word-boundary `company_match()` the prep path already used (the #497 fix), so both paths match identically and the divergent matcher is gone. A renamed `connections.csv` header now fails the same way at ingest as at prep — logging a `find_contacts_error` event instead of silently yielding zero contacts (no more silent split-brain). No schema change.

### Migration required

- **Schema 0010 — `jobs.network_depth` dropped** (#964): the dead contacts-count column is removed via `migrations/0010_drop_network_depth.sql`. It held `min(len(contacts), 2)` written at ingest but read by nothing (no SELECT, filter, or template — confirmed by a repo-wide sweep); the last writer is removed in the same change. **Auto-applied on next startup — no operator action, no data loss.** Fresh installs never carry the column.

## [0.32.0] — 2026-06-02

### Added

- **On-demand study guide + flashcard generation from the materials page** (#873): interview-stage jobs now get "Generate Study Guide" and "Generate Flashcards" buttons on `/materials/{fp}/`, extending the per-format podcast pattern from #870 to the other study artifacts. An operator juggling several interviews can regenerate just the flashcards for one job, or just the study guide for another, without re-running the full interview-prep pipeline (which rebuilds prep notes + study guide + flashcards + podcast as a bundle). Each button reuses the existing prep artifacts (briefing, tailored resume, cover, interview prep) as input; generation is non-destructive (timestamped output, existing files preserved) and gated by the spend ceiling (launch gate + per-call gate) plus a per-job concurrency guard via a `background_tasks` row — a double-click can't fire two paid runs. The generators were extracted into standalone `generate_study_guide_for_job` / `generate_flashcards_for_job` functions (mirroring `generate_podcast_for_job`) that the post-interview-prep bundled path now also delegates to, so the two code paths can't drift; as a side effect, a study-guide failure in the bundled path no longer blocks flashcard generation (they were coupled by an early return). New routes `POST /materials/{fp}/study-guide` and `POST /materials/{fp}/flashcards`.

- **Keyboard/screen-reader focus management for board action panels** (#944): The board's HTMX cell-swap panels (add-exclusion-rule, reattribute, generic confirm, and the change-reason `<select>` re-render) now move keyboard focus when they open and return it when they close. Builds directly on #886's `role="group"` panel markers: a small global `htmx:afterSettle` handler (`static/focus_panels.js`) reads the live swapped-in `<td>` (`evt.detail.elt` — not the detached `evt.detail.target`), and on open moves focus to the labelled panel **container** via `tabindex="-1"` rather than its first control, so a screen reader announces the panel's purpose and no destructive button (e.g. the confirm modal's "Confirm", which deletes a `feedback_log` row or re-runs paid prep) is pre-armed. The generic confirm modal — previously `aria-label="Confirm action"`, which would have announced only that generic label on focus — now labels its container via `aria-labelledby` pointing at the warning copy (and any context lines), scoped by a `modal_id` (the job fingerprint) the callers pass, so focusing it actually reads out the consequence being confirmed. On cancel/submit — or when a change-reason select re-renders itself — focus returns to the restored cell's first interactive control instead of being stranded on `<body>`. Scoped to `<td>`-level swaps, so row-level actions (`closest tr`) and the dashboard `/rows` refresh never hijack focus. Focus landing on exclude/reattribute/confirm/change-reason verified via `document.activeElement`; the real VoiceOver/NVDA announcement smoke is the one acceptance check that requires a live screen reader.

- **`/docs/updating` page** (#910, part of epic #923): New "How to update findajob" doc covering the three update paths — Fly (`fly deploy --config ops/fly.toml`), Docker with Watchtower (automatic within an hour), and Docker without Watchtower (`docker compose pull && docker compose up -d`) — what an update preserves (everything in `state/`: data, config, interview answers, prep materials), and how to check the running version. Registered in the `/docs/` route allowlist and the container-integration smoke slug loop.

### Changed

- **Onboarding timezone is now applied** (#981): the timezone captured during onboarding (written to `data/timezone`) was never read — the effective zone was only ever the deploy-config `TZ`. The container entrypoint now reads `data/timezone` at boot and exports it as `TZ`, overriding the deploy default, so the operator's pick drives cron timing (triage, notifications) and all displayed times. Because `TZ` is read at container start, the pick takes effect on the next restart; the dashboard shows a dismissible "Restart to apply your timezone" banner until it does (and auto-clears once applied). No schema change.
- **CI and Docker image builds now install from the committed `uv.lock`** (#961): both surfaces previously resolved dependency `>=` floors fresh from PyPI at build time (`pip install -e ".[dev]"` in CI, `pip install -e .` in the image), so the lockfile gave no reproducibility or supply-chain protection — a yanked or compromised upstream release satisfying a floor would land in the auto-pulled `:latest` image with the lockfile unused. `uv.lock` is also now **tracked** (it had been gitignored in `4194b2a` on the rationale "nothing in CI/Docker consumes it" — this is the change that gives it a consumer; supersedes that commit). CI and the image's throwaway `deps` build stage run `uv export --locked …` to produce a pinned, hashed requirements file that `pip install --require-hashes` consumes, then editable-install findajob with `--no-deps` (the project has no `[build-system]`, so it is excluded from the export via `--no-emit-project` and installed separately). `--locked` — not `--frozen` — is deliberate: `--frozen` silently uses a stale lock, while `--locked` fails the build loudly when `uv.lock` has drifted from `pyproject.toml`, satisfying the "drift fails loud" requirement. uv is pinned (`uv==0.11.7`) from PyPI in both surfaces, so the image needs no external uv image tag and the runtime image stays uv-free. No deploy-procedure change — operators pull the rebuilt image as usual; the dependency *set* is unchanged, only its resolution is now pinned. Maintenance consequence: a `pyproject` dependency change must be accompanied by `uv lock`, or CI fails until the lockfile is regenerated.
- **GitHub Actions runtime bump ahead of the 2026-06-02 node-20 cutover** (#835): `docker/setup-qemu-action@v3 → @v4` (in `build-image.yml`) and `actions/setup-python@v5 → @v6` (in `ci.yml`) — the two action pins still declaring `runs.using: node20` after the #568 sweep, now on `node24`. The qemu pin is the one that surfaced a deprecation warning at the v0.27.10 tag build; setup-python would have warned identically once the cutover landed. The remaining pins (`actions/checkout@v5`, `docker/setup-buildx-action@v4`, `docker/login-action@v4`, `docker/build-push-action@v7`) already ship `node24` and were left unchanged. No `FORCE_JAVASCRIPT_ACTIONS_TO_NODE24` opt-in needed — both bumps had node24 releases available. `setup-python@v6` carries no behavioral change beyond the runtime (its only breaking change is the node-24 upgrade itself, with a runner-version floor GitHub-hosted runners already clear).
- **Deferred UX copy polish — settings, errors, empty states** (#919, #920): Completes the #917 follow-up by carrying the canonical "your findajob" phrasing into the Settings pages (active sources, backup, connections, remove-confirm) in place of "this stack". The reject-reasons "title-signal" checkbox is relabeled to plain "Title looked right, job wasn't" (the internal term preserved in a tooltip); the excluded-employers Regex section is marked "(advanced)" and leads with the exact-match default; the Tools "Run a job now" heading becomes "Run pipeline steps"; and the onboarding interview "Configuration error" label becomes "Setup issue". Empty states and the apply toast gain context (#920): Materials "None." becomes "No materials in this stage yet." / "No rejected materials yet."; the board table "No matches." becomes "No jobs match your current filters."; the reattribute search "No matches." becomes "No jobs match your search."; and the apply undo toast "Applied. Folder moved and snapshot saved." becomes "Marked as applied." The "your findajob" sweep also covers every other user-facing "this stack" instance — the Gmail-disclosure banner, the onboarding connections-upload step, and the dashboard default-adapters banner — leaving the term only in code comments and literal command examples. Env-key validation messages are intentionally unchanged: they are operator-targeted, and manual key entry is already the primary action on failure.
- **Documentation v2 — core docs rewritten for a non-technical job-seeker audience** (epic #923): `getting-started/api-keys.md` leads with the one required account (OpenRouter), frames RapidAPI as optional with the consequence of skipping it spelled out, and moves legacy per-adapter env vars + pagination tuning behind an Advanced fold. `usage.md` drops the operator-only POST-handler/stage-name tables and the `/tools/` operator-controls section, keeping the daily-loop walkthrough and tab-by-tab guide. `CONTRIBUTING.md` slims to ~60 lines (dev setup, commit conventions, PR process) and points at `CLAUDE.md` and `architecture.md` for invariants and design rather than restating them. `maintainers/generalization.md` gains contributor-audience framing and trims shipped items to one line each. `operations/README.md` trims to the operator essentials with Docker+Fly command pairs; its script-reference section moves into `CLAUDE.md` § Scripts Reference so the operator audience and the agent audience read it from one place.
- **Opus 4.7 → 4.8 across all Opus-pinned roles** (#928): The eight roles that route to Anthropic Opus — `briefing_writer`, `resume_tailor`, `cover_letter_writer`, `recruiter_critic`, `interview_prep`, `outreach_drafter`, `voice_processor`, `podcast_scriptwriter` — now pin `openrouter:anthropic/claude-opus-4.8`. The 4.8 slug was verified against the live OpenRouter catalog: it launched at the same `$5/$25` per-Mtok tier as 4.7 (the `-fast` variant at `$10/$50` is deliberately not used), so there is no per-prep cost change. `config/model_pricing.yaml` gains a 4.8 rate row; the 4.7 row is retained so historical `cost_log` entries still price correctly. `tests/test_cost_tracking.py` asserts the 4.8 rate. Docs updated in lockstep (`docs/architecture.md` per-stage table and rationale, `getting-started/api-keys.md`, `CLAUDE.md` § Per-Role Model Assignments) plus code docstrings in `llm/openrouter.py` and `onboarding/voice_processor.py`. `pin_provider="anthropic"` cache-routing is unchanged — 4.8 is an Anthropic model reached through the same OpenRouter path, so cache_control behavior carries over. No migration required: role configs and the pricing table are baked into the image, so the change ships on a normal image pull. (Folds in #930, the narrow recruiter_critic bump.)
- **Onboarding copy humanized** (#917): Plain-English rewrite of the developer jargon every new user reads during onboarding. "Your seven config files are installed" → "Your profile and settings are saved"; "Discovery deferred to the weekly cron … the next Sunday 02:00 cron run" → "We'll look for companies automatically once a week … the next weekly run (Sunday mornings)"; "All required blocks have been emitted … write your config files atomically" → "Everything we need is ready … save your settings"; "this container's environment" / "this stack's `data/.env`" / "per-stack key isolation" → "your findajob". The length-error recovery message drops `max_tokens`/`emit` wording. Malformed-response errors no longer show the user the raw upstream body and "unexpected response shape" jargon: the interview-turn error and the Step 1 key-verification smoke check (which deliberately share wording) both now say a plain "Something unexpected happened. Try again." / "OpenRouter sent back a response findajob couldn't read…", with the diagnostic detail moved to a `logging.warning` for the operator. The jargon term `container` survives only in a literal `docker logs` command example. "your findajob" is adopted as the canonical phrasing the deferred per-surface polish (#919) will apply consistently elsewhere.

### Removed

- **`jobs.gdrive_folder_url` column** and its last writer (a `gdrive_folder_url=NULL` clause in `board_actions._regenerate`) — see *Migration required* above (#966).
- **Stale `analyze_feedback` mypy override** in `pyproject.toml`: the #558 extraction it guarded shipped (`scripts/analyze_feedback.py` is now a thin shim importing `findajob.analyze_feedback`), so the override suppressed nothing. (#966)

### Fixed

- **Stats windows bucketed on UTC days, not the operator's local day** (#967): the funnel, feedback, and scoring tabs computed "today" with `datetime.now(UTC).date()` and grouped transitions with `date(changed_at)`, so a transition made late in the operator's local evening (stored as the *next* UTC day) landed in the wrong daily bucket, contrary to the documented naïve-UTC-in-DB / local-calendar contract. A new `findajob.timeutil` module (`local_tz`, `local_zoneinfo`, `today_local`, `day_window_start_utc`, `utc_str_to_local_date`) centralizes reading the deployment's timezone — it resolves the `TZ` env var (any IANA zone; UTC fallback) and reuses the `astimezone(UTC)` idiom already proven DST-correct in `cost_rollups`. Funnel and feedback now fetch raw timestamps and bucket on the local calendar day in Python; scoring uses a local-midnight-in-UTC lower bound. Regression tests pin the late-evening-on-the-wrong-day scenario at both the helper and funnel-route level, across more than one region (`America/Los_Angeles`, `Asia/Tokyo`, `Europe/Berlin`). No schema change.
- **Display timestamps were hardcoded to Pacific time** (#967): several user-facing surfaces converted naïve-UTC timestamps with a literal `ZoneInfo("America/Los_Angeles")` rather than the deployment's configured zone — the notes-history disclosure, the regenerate confirm modal's "Last generated" line, the connections "Last imported" line, and the daily apply-reminder quip rotation (which changed at Pacific midnight regardless of the operator's region). All now resolve the zone through `findajob.timeutil.local_zoneinfo()`, so an operator in any timezone sees times on their own clock; the `updated_at_pt` / `last_imported_pt` template keys were renamed `_local` to match. Behavior for Pacific-configured deployments is unchanged. No schema change.
- **Recall-audit page labeled per-date rows as "Week"** (#967): the route groups by `date(audited_at)` — one row per audit *run*, dated by when it ran — but the template called every row a "Week", which misreads the moment the audit runs twice in one week. The column header, section header, chart aria-label, and explainer copy now say "audit date"; the `weeks`/`w` identifiers were renamed `audits`/`a` to match. No grouping change — the cron stays weekly, but the displayed grain is honestly per-date.
- **Approving a duplicate `[SPEC]` role returned a 500; synthetic rows skipped Tier-2 dedup** (#967): the speculative approver wrote `jobs.fingerprint` but never `loose_fingerprint`, so synthetic rows silently bypassed loose (title+company) de-duplication; and re-approving a request whose `[SPEC]` role collided with an existing fingerprint raised an unhandled `IntegrityError` → 500. The approver now populates `loose_fingerprint` from the same helper real rows use, and catches `IntegrityError` per card — skipping the duplicate and continuing to write the remaining new cards (SQLite `ABORT` rolls back only the offending statement, not the transaction). `approved_role_count` now reflects rows actually written. Regression tests cover the loose-fingerprint write and a cross-request duplicate that keeps the new card. No schema change. (Also: `tests/test_actions.py` was migrated off its hand-rolled schema onto the shared `init_test_db()` migration runner (#721), which immediately surfaced that production `jobs.source` is `NOT NULL` with no default.)
- **Un-apply restored a stage the job was never in** (#959): `un_apply_job` hard-coded the restore to `materials_drafted`, but `apply()` is reachable from `briefing_ready` (Phase B skipped) as well as `materials_drafted` — so undoing an apply on a briefing-only job landed it in `materials_drafted`, implying a tailored resume / cover / critique that don't exist, and the dashboard then offered actions premised on full materials. It now restores the actual prior stage from `audit_log` (the most recent `… → applied` row's `old_value`, ordered `changed_at DESC, id DESC`), with `materials_drafted` as the final fallback — matching the un-interview / un-withdraw / promote-from-fallback handlers. This depended on #958: apply's stage change + audit row now commit atomically, so the `… → applied` row is reliably present to read. Regression tests (`tests/test_actions.py::TestUnApplyJob`) cover restoration from `briefing_ready` and `materials_drafted`, the no-audit fallback, and the most-recent-wins tiebreaker on a re-apply cycle. (Also corrected: the hand-rolled `tests/test_actions.py` schema's `stage` CHECK had drifted — it was missing `briefing_ready`, which the real migrated schema carries.) No schema change.
- **Stage changes committed without their audit row; restoration had no tiebreaker** (#958): every stage transition wrote the `jobs.stage` UPDATE and its `audit_log` row as *two separate commits* (`write_audit` does its own INSERT+commit). A crash between the two left a job durably at the new stage with no audit trail — which then breaks the reverse handlers (they fall back to `applied`) and the un-apply 30s window (no `… → applied` row to find). Every transition site now commits the stage change and its audit row in a single transaction: the `actions.py` reverse/handle functions drop the pre-`write_audit` commit and let the last `write_audit` flush both; `board_actions._transition_stage` does the same; and the #957 prep-claim path folds the audit INSERT *inside* `_claim_prep_slot`'s claim transaction (under the same RESERVED lock, one commit) so the atomic-claim guarantee is preserved while closing the window. Separately, prior-stage restoration used `ORDER BY changed_at DESC LIMIT 1` with no `id` tiebreaker; `changed_at` is second-resolution naive text, so two transitions to the same target within one clock-second could restore the wrong `old_value`. All five restoration lookups (`un_not_selected`, `un_withdraw`, `un_interview`, and both hops of `promote_from_fallback`) now order by `changed_at DESC, id DESC` so the most recent transition wins on a tie. Regression tests (`tests/test_audit_atomicity.py`) prove the stage stays unchanged when the audit write raises (fresh-connection read) and that restoration picks the highest-id row on a `changed_at` tie; handler tests assert exactly one stage→`prep_in_progress` audit row (no duplicate from the fold). No schema change.
- **Backup-restore symlink escape** (#960): the restore extractor hand-rolled tar extraction and called `os.symlink(member.linkname, dest)` with no validation of the link *target* — `_is_path_safe` checked only the member's own name, never where a symlink pointed. A crafted tarball that passed `validate_tarball` (valid `pipeline.db` + `.onboarding-complete`) could carry a symlink member targeting an absolute path (`/etc`, `/app/data/.env`) or a `../`-escape and have it created outside the state root after the atomic swap, enabling arbitrary-path read/overwrite inside the container. Reachable unauthenticated via `POST /onboarding/restore/upload` in the fresh-deploy, pre-onboarding window where the auth middleware is fail-open. Because `backup.py` only ever tars regular files and directories — the pipeline creates no symlinks anywhere in the codebase — any link member is anomalous by construction, so the extractor now **refuses the whole restore** on encountering a symlink or hardlink member rather than validating targets (no link materialized means no target-validation bypass to find). The `os.symlink` call is gone. Regression tests (`tests/test_restore.py`) feed crafted tarballs with a relative-escape symlink, an absolute-target symlink, and a symlink-then-write-through payload, asserting refusal and that no escaping path is created; the legitimate-restore happy path stays green. No schema change — bugfix to the extractor only.
- **Prep-launch was a non-atomic check-then-act — a double-click could double prep spend** (#957): every prep-launching handler (`prep`, `regenerate`, `continue_prep`, `reactivate_and_prep`, and the `/materials/` regenerate + continue-prep wrappers) read the job's stage and the in-flight count, then *separately* wrote `prep_in_progress` and spawned `prep_application.py`. Two near-simultaneous requests (an operator double-click, an HTMX retry) both passed the guards before either wrote, so both launched a Phase-A run for one job — doubling the LLM spend the guard exists to prevent — and the 3-job cross-job concurrency cap could be exceeded under burst flagging. The check and the write now collapse into one conditional statement, `board_actions._claim_prep_slot`: `UPDATE jobs SET stage='prep_in_progress' … WHERE id=? AND stage <claimable> AND (SELECT COUNT(*) … WHERE stage='prep_in_progress') < MAX`, launching only when `rowcount == 1`. The claim is the *first* state mutation in every handler, so the destructive `regenerate` folder delete and every subprocess launch run only for the winner. `reactivate_and_prep` now claims straight from `waitlisted → prep_in_progress` and relocates the prep folder inline (the prior `handle_reactivate`-first flow wrote a two-row `waitlisted → intermediate → prep_in_progress` audit trail; that is intentionally collapsed to a single row — see #958 for the audit-row work). Regression test (`tests/test_prep_atomic_claim.py`) drives concurrent claims through threads against per-request connections — `TestClient` can't produce true request concurrency — and asserts exactly one winner and that the cap holds under burst. No schema change — bugfix to the web write surface only.

- **Migration runner per-migration atomicity was a no-op** (#954): the apply loop wrapped each migration in `conn.execute("BEGIN")` … `conn.executescript(sql)` … `except: conn.rollback()`, but `executescript()` issues an implicit `COMMIT` before running — so the `BEGIN` was committed away and the statements ran in autocommit, leaving `rollback()` nothing to undo. A migration that failed partway (interruption, OOM, disk-full, or a non-idempotent statement re-running on a partial DB) could permanently brick boot — most exposed on fresh installs replaying `0001→0009` from scratch with no `IF NOT EXISTS` self-heal on `0006`/`0007`. Transaction control now lives *inside* the script `executescript` runs (`BEGIN; <sql> <schema_version stamp>; COMMIT;`), with the version bump folded into the same transaction so a migration's statements and its version row commit or roll back as one unit. The module docstring (which had advertised the guarantee the code didn't provide) now describes the real mechanism. Regression test (`tests/test_db_migrate.py::test_failing_migration_leaves_nothing_applied`) proves a failing second statement leaves zero rows applied and the version unbumped. No schema change — bugfix to the runner only.

- **`/stats/config-change/{date}` popover 500** (#953): `metrics/stats.py`'s before/after cost query filtered on `cost_log.timestamp`, a column that does not exist — the real column is `logged_at` (as `cost_rollups.py` uses everywhere). Every config-change marker popover on the funnel/feedback/throughput charts returned a 500. A unit fixture that hand-rolled a fabricated `cost_log` schema with a `timestamp` column kept the suite green over the production break (the `feedback_test_real_codepath_when_extracting` anti-pattern, #610/#611, recurring); the test now builds the real schema via `init_test_db`, and a new route-level regression test (`tests/test_web_stats_config_change.py`) asserts the popover returns 200.


- **Recurring-themes floor scales with corpus size + display cap** (#932): On the real 62-company corpus the recruiter-critique aggregate (#265) emitted ~96 recurring themes — ordinary critique vocabulary ("vague", "metrics", "filler") trivially cleared the flat floor of 3 distinct companies, burying signal in noise. The source-level clusters were unaffected (they anchor to a real `file:line`); only the unanchored-themes surface was over-broad. The two floors are now decoupled: source clusters keep the flat `--min-companies` floor (default 3), while the themes floor scales with the corpus-wide distinct-company count via `default_theme_floor(n) = max(8, ceil(0.15 * n))` (e.g. 10 on a 62-company corpus). A new `--min-theme-companies` CLI flag overrides the scaled default downward to inspect the long tail. On top of the floor, `render_report()` caps the rendered themes list at `DEFAULT_MAX_THEMES` (15) and surfaces any overflow as an explicit "… N more theme(s) below the displayed cap" line — never a silent drop. The `/tools/critique-review/` web view (#933) now imports the same `DEFAULT_MAX_THEMES` constant so the CLI report and the browser view share one cap and can't drift.
- **Stale `install-docker.md` links + undiscoverable docs pages** (#938): Two getting-started docs (`cost.md`, `install-fly.md`) still linked to a bare `install-docker.md` after #904 relocated the file into `docs/operations/`, resolving to a 404 in the in-app docs viewer; both now point at `../operations/install-docker.md`. Separately, `/docs/updating` (added in #910) and `/docs/tuning` were registered in the route allowlist but absent from the curated `_INDEX_GUIDES` list that renders the `/docs/` home, so a user landing on the docs index couldn't discover them — both now appear as index cards with one-line blurbs.

### Migration required

- **`background_tasks.kind` CHECK gains `study_guide` + `flashcards`** (#873): on-demand study-guide / flashcard generation records a `background_tasks` row per kind for the same double-submit + concurrency guard the podcast path uses (#879). The two values are added to the canonical CHECK in `migrations/0002_background_tasks.sql`, and an idempotent rebuild helper (`db/migrate._add_study_materials_kinds_if_needed`, mirroring `_add_podcast_kind_if_needed`) brings existing stacks up via the rename-create-copy-drop dance — SQLite has no `ALTER CHECK`. **Auto-applied on next startup — no operator action, no data loss, no `schema_version` bump** (constraint relaxation, invisible to the version counter). Fresh installs get the new CHECK directly from 0002.
- **Schema 0009 — `jobs.gdrive_folder_url` dropped** (#966): the dead Google Drive sync column is removed via `migrations/0009_drop_gdrive_folder_url.sql`. It held the per-job Drive folder link from the rclone/Drive materials-sync era, retired when the local web materials viewer shipped; it has been NULL in every row since and no code reads it. **Auto-applied on next startup — no operator action, no data loss.** Fresh installs never carry the column.

## [0.31.3] — 2026-05-30

### Added

- **Web view for the recruiter-critique aggregate** (#933): New `/tools/critique-review/` page renders the #265 aggregator output in the browser instead of requiring a CLI run + SSH. Computes the aggregate live on each load (fast — no LLM), and shows source-level fixes as cards (action badge · `file:line` · the source line · the recruiter's verbatim words · distinct-company chips, sorted by recurrence), a capped recurring-themes strip (top 15; the full themes-floor tuning is tracked in #932), and an empty state. Linked from the `/tools/` index. Read-only — unlike the CLI it does not write the dated report file. The page embeds real resume lines but the whole app is auth-gated, consistent with `/materials/`. The CLI and the web view share `default_source_files()` so the anchor labels can't drift between them.

## [0.31.2] — 2026-05-30

### Added

- **Recruiter-critique aggregator** (#265): New `scripts/critique_review.py` scans every `* Critique - *.md` artifact across the company folders and surfaces the weaknesses that recur across *different* applications — the ones that live at the source (`master_resume.md`, `profile.md`, role prompts) rather than in any one prep. Each flagged line is fuzzy-anchored back to the exact source line it came from (via `rapidfuzz`, so the critic's paraphrases still cluster instead of scattering into noise), then grouped by source line and ranked by **distinct-company count**. The dated markdown report (written to gitignored `candidate_context/critique_aggregate/<date>.md`, since it quotes real resume lines) has three parts: *Source-level fixes* (a line flagged by ≥3 companies, with `file:line`, the recruiter's verbatim words, and a count), *Recurring themes* (career-neutral term frequency across critiques — points at prompt/profile fixes with no single source line), and a collapsed *One-offs* count. No LLM runs in the aggregator — the recruiter's own Opus-authored voice carries through by quotation; the tool only supplies the index. Flags: `--since`, `--min-companies`, `--print`. Run manually after ~10+ preps accumulate.

### Fixed

- **`withdrew` stage drift broke the Archive stage filter and withdrawn-job re-ingest dedup** (#894): The `jobs.stage` CHECK constraint only ever stores `withdrawn`, but two code paths referenced a non-existent `withdrew` value. (1) `_STAGE_VALUES` in `findajob.web.filters.registry` offered `withdrew` as a Stage-column enum option, so the Archive tab's `?stage=withdrawn` filter passed `withdrew` into the WHERE clause and matched zero rows. (2) `_APPLIED_STAGES` in `findajob.ingest` listed `withdrew`, so a withdrawn job that was re-ingested was treated as a fresh resurface instead of being recognized as already-applied. Both now use the DB-canonical `withdrawn`. A new regression test inserts every `_STAGE_VALUES` entry against the real migrated schema (the CHECK constraint as oracle), so any future display-vs-DB stage drift fails loudly instead of silently matching zero rows. Also folded in: `_APPLIED_STAGES` was missing `withdrawn_fallback` (#358) entirely — re-ingesting a job parked in the fallback queue bumped its score and overwrote fields instead of reporting already-applied (the stage itself was preserved, so no queue eviction); `withdrawn_fallback` is now recognized as the post-application stage it is.

## [0.31.1] — 2026-05-29

### Fixed

- **Applied option missing from Dashboard dropdown for `briefing_ready` rows** (#924): After Phase A completed and the row settled at `briefing_ready`, the Dashboard dropdown only exposed Waitlist — operators couldn't skip Phase B and apply with what Phase A produced without round-tripping through `/materials/`. `_status_cell.html` was gating the Applied option on `stage == 'materials_drafted'`; relaxed to also include `briefing_ready` (where there is no running subprocess, so the apply transition cannot race with an orchestrator stage write). The SPEC-row "Sent Outreach" label variant is preserved. `prep_in_progress` is intentionally left out — the prep orchestrator's stage-update SQL lacks a current-stage guard, so a finishing Phase B subprocess could silently flip an apply'd row back; a new test pins that exclusion in place.
- **Tier 1 parser silently disabled mis-score health check on table-formatted `target_companies.md`**: `parse_target_companies_tier1` in `findajob.config_loader` only recognized bullet/numbered list entries, so any `target_companies.md` that used a markdown table for the `## Tier 1` section parsed to an empty list. `load_companies_of_interest()` then returned an empty frozenset and `is_company_of_interest()` always returned False, silently disabling the daily `notify.py health-check` REVIEW line for target-company jobs scored 3–6. The parser now reads both bullets and markdown tables (header row detected by following `|---|` separator; first cell of each body row contributes the company name, with the same trailing-commentary stripping as bullets). Mixed bullet+table sections are supported.
- **Tier 1 parser silently failed to match `"Google / DeepMind"`-style multi-name entries**: An operator's "either of these" shorthand (`"Google / DeepMind"`, `"Anthropic / Claude"`) parsed to one Tier 1 entry whose substring never matched any real-world input — `"google / deepmind" in "google cloud"` is False, so the mis-score check missed every Google-titled job. The parser now splits cell contents on ` / ` (with surrounding whitespace) into multiple entries, emitting both `"Google"` and `"DeepMind"`. Slashes without surrounding whitespace (`"S&P/TSX"`, `"Boeing/Northrop"`) and `&`-joined names (`"Procter & Gamble"`, `"Johnson & Johnson"`) pass through untouched — the former are intentional single names; the latter are too common in real company names to risk splitting.

### Added

- **In-app auth credential setup during onboarding** (#895): New instances can set their HTTP Basic Auth username and password directly in the onboarding flow — no Fly CLI or terminal access needed. Credentials are written to `data/.env` and the auth middleware activates immediately without a container restart. The step is conditional: skipped when credentials are already set via Fly secrets or environment variables. Fly Secrets remain a valid alternative for users who prefer to set auth pre-deploy. Defense against drive-by password squat: a one-time setup token is written to container stdout on first boot and required in the auth-setup form — the operator reads it from `fly logs` / `docker logs`, an attacker hitting the public URL cannot. `verify_auth` now loads `data/.env` so it can verify credentials set via the onboarding flow.
- **Re-run interview prep button on materials page** (#875): Interview-stage jobs now show a "Re-run interview prep" button on `/materials/{fp}/`. Generates fresh study guide, flashcards, and interview notes — useful for jobs prepped before those features shipped, or after receiving panel info. Per-job concurrency guard via `background_tasks`; spend ceiling launch gate. Same subprocess as the dashboard "Interviewing" re-click.
- **Spend ceiling ntfy alerts at 80% and 100%** (#876): Both the per-call gate and launch gate now fire ntfy notifications when monthly LLM spend crosses 80% ("approaching ceiling") and 100% ("ceiling reached — calls blocked"). Alerts fire at most once per threshold per calendar month, deduped via in-process cache + `notifications` table query. Notification failure never breaks the safety gate. Two new notification kinds: `spend_ceiling_warning`, `spend_ceiling_reached`.
- **Auto-derive `FINDAJOB_WEB_URL` from Fly runtime env** (#881): On Fly.io, `FINDAJOB_WEB_URL` is now auto-derived from the `FLY_APP_NAME` env var (set by Fly at runtime) when not explicitly configured. Eliminates 1 required secret from Fly deploys. Fallback chain: `data/.env` → `FINDAJOB_WEB_URL` env → `https://{FLY_APP_NAME}.fly.dev` → `http://localhost:8090`. `fly-deploy.sh` now marks `FINDAJOB_WEB_URL` as optional (skippable).
- **Root-level `fly.toml` for web deploy** (#881): Tracked `fly.toml` at repo root enables the Fly.io "Launch from GitHub" web flow with default config path `./`. CLI users continue using `ops/fly.toml.example` → `ops/fly.toml` unchanged.
- **Gem GraphQL adapter** (#249): New `GemAdapter` fetches job postings from Gem-hosted boards (`jobs.gem.com`) via the public GraphQL batch endpoint. Two-phase fetch: list query + per-posting detail call for descriptions. No auth required. Opt-in via `config/active_sources.txt` (not auto-enabled).

## [0.31.0] — 2026-05-27

### Added

- **Server-side podcast generation progress tracking** (#879): Podcast generation now records state in the `background_tasks` table instead of relying on client-side Alpine.js state. "Generating..." indicator survives page refresh. Per-job duplicate guard prevents concurrent podcast generation for the same job. Watchdog reaps stuck podcast tasks after 30 min. New `writeback_sync` context manager in `findajob.background_tasks` — generalizable helper for synchronous in-handler long-running work (counterpart to `writeback_subprocess` for subprocess-based tasks). Error banner surfaces `already_generating`, `spend_ceiling`, and `generation_failed` states.

### Migration required

- `background_tasks.kind` CHECK constraint expanded to include `'podcast'`. Applied automatically by the migration runner at container start (idempotent table rebuild, same pattern as `prep_phase_b`).

## [0.30.1] — 2026-05-27

### Fixed

- **Speculative prep always failed validation** — `candidate_led_briefing` role lacked the "Overall Recommendation" section that the Phase A validator requires. When prep reused the speculative briefing (bypassing `briefing_writer`), validation failed with "briefing: missing Overall Recommendation" and reset the job to `scored`. Added the section to the role prompt with Pursue/Pass vocabulary appropriate for cold-outreach context.
- **Speculative briefing truncation** — `candidate_led_briefing` (sonar-deep-research) and `company_researcher` (sonar-reasoning-pro) were using the default `max_tokens: 4096`, too low for reasoning models that produce verbose multi-section output. Raised both to `max_tokens: 16384`.

## [0.30.0] — 2026-05-27

### Added

- **Un-interview — reverse an interview stage transition** (#893): `POST /board/jobs/{fp}/un-interview` restores the prior stage from `audit_log` (fallback `applied`). Applied tab dropdown surfaces "Undo Interview" when `stage=interview`. Row stays on Applied tab with OOB stage-change toast. No migration required.

- **Fallback queue for withdrew-but-might-revisit jobs** (#358): New `withdrawn_fallback` stage and dedicated `/board/fallback` tab. Operators can mark jobs as fallback-eligible from the Applied tab dropdown ("Withdrew (Fallback)") or convert existing withdrawn rows from the Archive tab ("Fallback" button). The Fallback tab shows title, company, withdraw reason, date, relevance score, location, and notes. Jobs can be promoted back to their prior stage (applied/interview/offer) or rejected directly. No folder moves — rows stay in `_applied/`. Existing withdrawn rows are not auto-migrated. Schema migration: `_rebuild_table_with_indexes` relaxes the `jobs.stage` CHECK constraint and the `view_prefs.tab` CHECK constraint (idempotent, applied automatically at next container start).

- **Two-speaker interview-prep podcasts** (#870): Gemini TTS integration renders conversational audio podcasts from prep artifacts. Four formats: Deep Dive (auto-generated with interview prep), Q&A Drill, Critical Analysis, and The Brief (on-demand from `/materials/`). New `findajob.llm.tts` module wraps the Google AI API `MultiSpeakerVoiceConfig` endpoint; scripts longer than ~2 min use segment-and-stitch for quality. Spend-ceiling two-point enforcement. Materials page shows embedded `<audio>` players + download buttons per format. Requires `GEMINI_API_KEY` env var (optional; free tier sufficient). `ffmpeg` added to Docker image. New role prompt: `podcast_scriptwriter` (Sonnet 4.6). Cost: ~$0.13 (Brief) to $0.42 (Extended) per podcast — Opus 4.7 scriptwriter + Gemini 3.1 Flash TTS.
- **Study guide + Anki flashcard deck** (#869): Interview-prep flow now generates a structured study guide (`{prep_folder}/Study Guide - *.md`) and a flashcard deck (`.apkg` for Anki, `.csv` for Quizlet) after the primary interview-prep artifact. Materials page renders an interactive fullscreen flashcard viewer (Alpine.js; arrow keys, space to flip, tag filter, shuffle). Two new role prompts: `study_guide_generator` (Sonnet 4.6) and `flashcard_generator` (Sonnet 4.6). Incremental cost ~$0.02/package. Dependency: `genanki>=0.13.0`.
- **Tuning loop Phase 2+3** (#230): Statistical rigor on all `/stats/*` pages — Wilson 95% CIs on every proportion, min-N=20 gating (strata below threshold render "—"), per-source stratification on `/stats/scoring`. Config-change vertical markers on trend charts (funnel, feedback, throughput) with click-to-compare before/after popover via `/stats/config-change/{date}` API. New `/stats/effectiveness` page (apply-to-response rate, interview rate, ghost rate, per-source breakdown, response latency). New `/stats/recall-audit` page + weekly `recall_audit` cron (samples 40 hard-rejected/low-scored jobs, re-scores with Sonnet 4.6, alerts at >10% upgrade rate). Daily `drift_alert` cron (fires ntfy 7 days after a config change when reject rate shifts >15pp or cost shifts >25%). `docs/tuning.md` user-facing guide. Statistical helpers module at `src/findajob/metrics/stats.py`.

### Changed

- **Onboarding interviewer Phase 5** (#833): auto-emit all config-file groups in one response instead of pausing for `next` between each group. Removes 8 confirmation gates; `redo {a|b|c|d}` remains active until Finalize. Voice-sample users with >5000 words of prose may see groups a–c and d split across two messages to avoid output truncation.

## [0.29.0] — 2026-05-24

### Added

- **Tuning loop Phase 1** (#229): `config_changes` and `recall_audit` tables; `jobs.company_tier` and `jobs.scored_by` columns; config-drift detector wired into triage, `/config/` POST, and onboarding injector; tier resolver; backfill scripts.

### Migration required

- Schema: run `scripts/init_db.py` on upgrade (auto-runs at container start). Backfill existing rows: `uv run python scripts/backfill_company_tier.py && uv run python scripts/backfill_scored_by.py` (both idempotent).

## [0.28.0] — 2026-05-24

### Changed

- **#815 chore: scrub operator-internal context from public repo.** Removed the `/admin/stacks/` multi-tenant operator dashboard (module, routes, templates, tests, `FINDAJOB_OPERATOR_MODE` env var). Deleted `docs/maintainers/tester-migration.md`, `docs/maintainers/release-parity-matrix.md`; removed operator-specific release-process content. Renamed all "tester" language to "user" in comments, docstrings, and docs (~70 files). Renamed DB columns `tester_openrouter_key` → `user_openrouter_key` and `tester_rapidapi_key` → `user_rapidapi_key` (migration 0006). Extracted `findajob.jsonl_tail` from the deleted admin module for continued use by `/tools/` log viewer. **Migration required** — see entry below.

- **#649 docs(release-process): rewrite as fork-friendly universal process.** `docs/maintainers/release-process.md` re-created as a 176-line universal doc covering version scheme, pre-tag checklist, CHANGELOG workflow, tag cut, post-tag verification, rollback, and `migration-required` criteria. No operator-specific topology, no deployment choreography for specific stacks — the release is complete when multi-arch images land on GHCR; how you deploy is documented in the install guides. Updated stale references in `install-docker.md`, `roadmap.md`, and `scripts/test_container_integration.sh`.

### Migration required

- **#815** — Migration 0006 renames two `onboarding_sessions` columns. The migration runner applies it automatically on next container start (via `scripts/init_db.py` in `ops/entrypoint.sh`). No manual SQL required; `_meta.schema_version` advances from 5 → 6. No data is lost — `RENAME COLUMN` is a DDL-only operation.

### Added

- **#830 feat(web): visible confirmation toast after stage transitions on `/board/applied` (and inverse routes).** Closes the gap `#779`'s `action_without_confirmation` rubric flagged at high confidence against findajob-staging on `applied_to_interviewing_undo` and `interviewing_to_offer_path` — six post-applied transition routes (`/interview`, `/offer`, `/withdraw`, `/not-selected`, `/un-withdraw`, `/un-not-selected`) now emit a `templates/board/_stage_change_toast.html` OOB swap into the existing `#undo-toast` placeholder (#699 infrastructure), reading "Stage changed to {Pretty(stage)}." with a 30s auto-dismiss + ✕ button (no Undo — none of these routes have a 30s-window inverse). For row-re-rendering routes (`/interview`, `/offer`) the response is `<tr>` + OOB toast; for empty-body routes (the other four) the response is just the OOB toast, matching `/apply`'s shape. The inverse routes (`un_withdraw_job`, `un_not_selected_job`) already returned the restored stage, so the toast text reflects the actual landed stage rather than hardcoding "Applied" — `un-not-selected` from a row that was at `offer` reads "Stage changed to Offer." accurately. Scope was deliberately bounded: `/un-apply` keeps its own 30s undo-toast pattern (#699, different shape); change-reason routes (`/change-reject-reason`, `/change-not-selected-reason`) are excluded because the inline dropdown value IS the confirmation; cross-tab transitions (`/promote`, `/reactivate`, `/waitlist`, `/reject`, `/un-reject`) weren't flagged by `#779`'s Applied-tab rubric and would dilute the PR. 9 new response-shape tests in `TestStageChangeToastOOB` assert positive containment (toast markers, stage label) paired with negative containment (no Undo button, no `/un-apply` posthook leak, no toast on 404) per `feedback_negative_test_assertions`; 4 existing tests on the changed routes updated from `assert response.text == ""` to the new toast-shape assertion. **No `migration-required`** — additive template + response-shape change; no schema, env var, or config-file shape change.

- **#841 feat(web): in-app backup/restore for platform-agnostic stack portability.** One-click backup tarball download from `/settings/backup/` (streams a gzipped tar via `sqlite3 .backup` API + `tarfile`). Restore via `/onboarding/restore/` accepts a backup tarball upload, validates the `state/` contract, and extracts atomically with rollback — skipping the interview for returning users. (#860, #861, #862: follow-up fixes for cross-filesystem bind-mount dirs, staging-dir placement, and Docker EBUSY on dir rename.)

- **#853 feat(fetchers): free public contract/gig job feed adapters.** Phase 1+2: Remote OK, Himalayas, We Work Remotely, Remotive, Jobicy. Phase 3: Algora Bounties, HN Firebase. All implement `JobSourceAdapter` protocol; opt-in via `config/active_sources.txt`.

- **#653 feat(web): per-row 'Add exclusion rule' affordance on `/board/dashboard`.** New 🚫 button in a `Rule` column on the dashboard tab opens a cell-swap modal asking the locus question — title-only vs JD-content — and writes a deterministic exclusion rule to the right gitignored config. Title-only routes to `config/prefilter_rules.yaml` `hard_rejects.operator_added` (Stage 1 in `scorer_prefilter` — title regex → score 1, no LLM call). JD-content routes to `candidate_context/profile.md` `## Excluded Categories` (read by the LLM scorer for content signals). Two new savers in `findajob.config_loader`: `add_prefilter_title_pattern(pattern, category)` appends to `hard_rejects[category]` with `re.compile` validation, duplicate detection, and atomic `os.replace`; `append_profile_excluded_category(entry)` appends a prose paragraph at the end of the section (before the next `## H2` or EOF) with duplicate-substring detection and atomic write. Modal mirrors the regenerate-confirm cell-swap pattern (#700) — `GET /board/jobs/{fp}/exclude/modal` swaps the cell with the form, `POST /board/jobs/{fp}/exclude` validates and applies and returns the icon cell, `GET /board/jobs/{fp}/exclude/cell` is the Cancel-restore. Title field pre-populates with a word-boundary regex draft from the row's title (`\bsenior\s+sales\s+engineer\b` style) that the operator edits before commit — the draft is a starting point, not a finished rule; word-boundary anchoring satisfies the #497 invariant. Rendered only on `/board/dashboard` — review / applied / waitlist / rejected tabs deferred until operator pain shows up. Generalization gate is satisfied by construction: the savers do not introspect tracked role files, so re-domain-locking the repo through operator-added content is impossible. Tests: 18 unit tests on the savers (atomic write, validation, duplicate, error paths) + 12 integration tests on the route (happy paths both loci, validation failures, 404s, locus dispatch). YAML `#` comments are not preserved across `add_prefilter_title_pattern` writes — consistent with `save_excluded_employers`'s round-trip behavior; the docstring documents the loss. The original #653 framing (M1 cluster sampler → M2 locus picker → M3 three-gate preview with FN-gate + soft-floor + `audit_log`) was explicitly downscoped during a YAGNI audit; deferred features documented in the updated issue body under `## Deferred — may revisit if pain shows up`, no speculative successor issue filed. **No `migration-required`** — additive route + saver pair; no schema change, no env var, no config-file shape change (operator-added entries are first-class members of existing `hard_rejects` and `## Excluded Categories` shapes).

### Fixed

- **#844 fix(web/filters): chip-strip ✕ buttons and "Clear all" no longer silently loop back to persisted state.** The #277 filter framework's chip-strip rendered ✕ buttons and the Clear-all link as `<a href="?…">` anchors that, when removing the last filter, landed on an empty URL. The route handler then saw `parsed.is_empty()`, the cold-load branch of `_maybe_redirect_to_persisted` fired, and the 303 sent the operator back to the persisted state they'd just tried to clear — visually indistinguishable from "the click did nothing". Symptom-C of the same bug class: the blue `cols: …` pill rendered any time `parsed.cols` was truthy, including when `cols` matched the spec's `default_visible` set, so toggling the Columns dropdown Apply with defaults checked persisted `cols=<defaults>` and made the pill permanent on the operator's perceived default view. Fix is two-part. (1) Template ✕ buttons in `_active_filters.html` are now POST forms targeting a new `POST /board/{tab}/reset-filter/{name}` route (and Clear-all targets the existing `/reset-view`). The new route reads persisted state, drops the named key, re-serializes with `default_cols`, and 303-redirects to the path with the remaining filters in the URL — explicit state mutation, no cold-load round-trip. `name` may be a column name (text/numeric/enum/date), the literal `cols`, or the literal `sort`. Unknown `name` is a deliberate no-op so stale forms after a rename don't 500; unknown `tab` is a 404. (2) `view_prefs.serialize()` gains an optional `default_cols=` kwarg — when `parsed.cols` set-equals `default_cols`, the `cols=` clause is dropped from the serialized string. `_persist_view` derives the per-tab defaults from `_STORAGE_TAB_SPECS` and passes them through, so no callers had to change. The chip-strip's cols pill rendering condition switched from `{% if parsed.cols %}` to a defaults comparison in `_active_filters.html`. Dead code removed: `filter_remove_qs` in `findajob.web.helpers` and its Jinja global registration (was only used by the chip ✕ anchors that no longer exist). Test coverage: 18 new tests across `tests/test_view_prefs.py` (six unit tests on the new `default_cols` behavior — exact match, set-equal regardless of order, subset/superset stays persisted, legacy callers without the kwarg unaffected, composite with other filters) and `tests/test_web_view_prefs_cascade.py` (twelve route-level tests: per-key clears preserve other filters, solo-chip clears reset the row entirely, cold-load after reset does NOT snap back, cols pill rendering gated by defaults comparison, chip ✕ buttons are POST forms not GET anchors, hyphenated `not-selected` tab URL routes correctly, unknown name no-ops, unknown tab returns 404). Out-of-band seven-tab curl-based clickthrough audit returned 75 PASS / 0 FAIL across dashboard, applied, review, waitlist, rejected, not-selected, archive. End-to-end Playwright spot-check confirmed the originally-reported operator behavior: cols pill ✕ navigates to bare `/board/dashboard`, no snap-back, pill disappears; Columns dropdown Apply with defaults persists no row and renders no pill. **No `migration-required`** — web/UI change, no schema/env/config.

## [0.27.11] — 2026-05-23

### Added

- **#816 feat(migrate): docker → Fly.io tester-stack migration tool.** New package `src/findajob/migrate/` with CLI `python -m findajob.migrate {export,import-fly,verify}` for moving a tester's accumulated state (SQLite database + `companies/` job-folder tree + `candidate_context/` persona profile and role artifacts) from `/opt/stacks/findajob-<handle>/state/` on the deployment host into a freshly-provisioned Fly app's volume. Two-phase orchestration per the advisor architectural review: source stack stopped → `PRAGMA wal_checkpoint(TRUNCATE)` + verify clean → tarball with embedded `manifest.json` (per-table row counts on `jobs`/`audit_log`/`feedback_log`/`cost_log`, SHA-256 of `pipeline.db`, file-count + total-size for `companies/` and `candidate_context/`); then `fly ssh sftp put` → `fly ssh console -C 'tar -xzf …'` → `fly ssh console -C 'python -m findajob.migrate verify …'` with JSON-parseable comparison against the embedded manifest. Stop-the-stack is enforced via the `DirtyWalError` refusal on non-empty WAL post-checkpoint — best-effort live snapshot would have required dozens of lines of race-defensive code for a one-shot per-tester cutover, which is the wrong tradeoff. Tolerance model: DB row counts and `pipeline.db` SHA-256 require **exact** match; `companies/` file count exact; `companies/` total size within **1%** to absorb filesystem block-size shift between deployment-host ext4 and Fly's ext4 volume; `candidate_context/` file count exact AND > 0. Idempotency: re-running import on a Fly volume that already has `manifest.json` aborts cleanly with `TargetNotEmptyError` (operator can pass `--force` to clobber). Excluded from the tarball on purpose: `aichat_ng/` (regenerable LLM chat state — historical interview chat replay does NOT survive migration) and `logs/` (rebuildable from pipeline events; inflates the tarball). Secrets are NOT in the runtime layer — operator hands them off separately via `fly secrets import < source/data/.env`, preserving the #339 per-stack key-isolation invariant. End-to-end dogfood against `findajob-staging` (1881 jobs / 5826 audit_log rows / 425 companies files / 8.7 MB tarball) → throwaway Fly app (`findajob-816-test`, since destroyed): 7.7 seconds wall-clock, `pipeline.db` SHA-256 byte-identical across the cutover (`1e61341e…`), all counts exact match. Runbook: [`docs/maintainers/tester-migration.md`](docs/maintainers/tester-migration.md). 44 unit tests (manifest round-trip + tolerance model, WAL checkpoint + dirty-WAL refusal, exporter tarball-shape + idempotency + checksum, importer orchestration with `FakeTransport` for every branch, verifier observation/comparison, CLI for all three subcommands). Routes SQLite through `findajob.db.connect` so the #548 invariant holds. **No `migration-required`** — additive package + tool; no schema migration, no env var, no config file, no behavior change in existing pipeline code paths. Gating prerequisite for #819 stack-stop checklist; downstream consumer of #749 cold-cutover playbook.

## [0.27.10] — 2026-05-23

### Fixed

- **#765 follow-up: `JobsApi14BingAdapter._compose_row` unwraps `/v2/bing/get`'s top-level `data` envelope (was reading fields directly off the response).** First-pass fix shipped under the original #765 entry below assumed the get-response was flat (`detail["applyUrl"]`); live capture against the operator's stack 2026-05-23 showed it's actually nested (`detail["data"]["applyUrl"]`, alongside `_links`, `errors`, `warnings`, `hasError`, `hasWarning`). Synthetic unit-test fixtures matched the flat assumption, so CI was green; production triage on the operator's stack produced zero rows across 5 queries (52 search rows → 0 composed). `_compose_row` now reads from `detail.get("data") or {}` with the `companyName` / `applyUrl` / `description` keys looked up on the unwrapped record. A separate defensive guard in `_call_with_retry` catches responses missing the `data` envelope (e.g. the `{"message": "...exceeded the rate limit per second..."}` shape captured during a transient PRO-tier burst) and emits `jobsapi_bing_unrecognized_response` log events with a body excerpt rather than passing through silently — the original #601/#765 silent-zero-rows failure class is exactly "unexpected response shape produces empty rows", and the loud-log makes the next variant immediately visible in `pipeline.jsonl`. Test suite gains three guards: `test_fetch_handles_recorded_real_get_response_shape` uses an inline recorded fixture (`_REAL_GET_RESPONSE_2026_05_23`) capturing the full envelope including `_links`/`errors`/`warnings`/`descriptionHtml` so a future "let me simplify the fixture" cleanup can't drift back to the flat-shape assumption; `test_fetch_logs_unrecognized_response_when_envelope_missing` exercises the `{"message": ...}` rate-limit shape and asserts both the empty-row outcome AND the loud-log emission with the rate-limit phrase preserved in the body excerpt; `test_recorded_get_response_is_real_envelope_shape` is a structural sanity-check that locks the recorded-fixture's outer keys (`data`, `hasError`, `errors`, `warnings`, `_links`, `hasWarning`) so the fixture itself stays representative. Also helper-extracts `_get_envelope(record, has_error=...)` so the remaining unit-test fixtures wrap their records under `data` automatically — keeps the test code readable while pinning the real shape. Module docstring updated with a "Response envelope" section pointing at the live-capture date. **No `migration-required`** — same internal-adapter-shape category as the original #765 fix; adapter remains opt-in-default-off.

- **#765 fix(adapters): `JobsApi14BingAdapter` follows the LinkedIn-shape two-call pattern (was Indeed-inline).** Surfaced during the #601 functional re-validation: `/v2/bing/search` returns lightweight summary rows; `applyUrl` + `description` + `companyName` only come back from `/v2/bing/get?id=<base64_id>`. The adapter's `_parse_rows()` was extracting `applyUrl` from the search response (where it doesn't exist), so every row had `url=""` and got dropped — first by the `if not url: continue` guard inside `_parse_rows`, and even if that passed, by `findajob.triage.orchestrator`'s empty-URL drop at intake. Net effect: the adapter was non-functional since shipping, but the bug was invisible because `jobs-api14-bing` is opt-in-default-off in `config/active_sources.txt` and no stack had enabled it. The fix inlines the get-call inside `fetch()` rather than deferring it to `findajob.fetchers.fetch_jd()` — that alternative would have been structurally broken because the orchestrator drops empty-URL rows before `fetch_jd` runs, so Bing rows would never reach the JD-fetch stage. Indeed shipped working because its search response really does carry everything inline; LinkedIn shipped working because its `linkedinUrl` is inline (only the JD body comes from its get-call). Bing is the unique case where both URL and JD live on get, hence the inline two-call. Split the adapter into `_parse_search_rows()` (extracts `id` + `title` + `location` hints from search), `_fetch_detail()` (per-id get-call), and `_compose_row()` (stitches hint + detail, consumes `companyName` from get — NOT `company` from search, which is the natural pitfall and explicitly guarded by a new regression test). `_call_with_retry` refactored to accept the endpoint URL as a parameter so both search and get inherit the 429 + Retry-After handling. Per-row `time.sleep(0.6)` between get-calls keeps the cost shape inside the PRO-tier 2 req/sec ceiling — for a query × location pair that yields 18 search rows (Bing's per-page cap), the fan-out is 1 search + 18 get calls = ~11 seconds wall-clock. `live_test()` stays single-call to `/v2/bing/search` so onboarding-time spot checks remain budget-bounded; counts reflect search-shape hits and are an approximation of fetch-shape rows, which is fine for the "is the Bing endpoint reachable" signal it provides. Test suite rewritten end-to-end: new `_two_call_side_effect` helper routes mocked `requests.get` calls by URL suffix so a single test can fixture both `/v2/bing/search` and per-id `/v2/bing/get` responses; new tests cover the stitching contract (`test_fetch_stitches_search_and_get_into_full_row`), the natural `companyName`-vs-`company` pitfall (`test_fetch_uses_companyName_not_company_key` — explicitly poisons the search-response `company` to "WRONG-KEY-VALUE" and asserts the row's `company` comes from get's `companyName`), the empty-`applyUrl` drop path (`test_fetch_drops_row_when_get_response_omits_applyUrl`), the search-stage filters that save wasted get-calls (`test_fetch_drops_rows_with_no_title_or_id_from_search`), single-bad-detail tolerance (`test_fetch_continues_when_one_get_call_fails`), and the pacing AC (`test_fetch_paces_get_calls_with_sleep`). Pre-existing tests updated for the two-call shape and kept green (regression-locked: title-allowlist contract, 429-retry, hasError-response). Module docstring rewritten — drops the "mirrors Indeed's payload" claim and the "operator's first triage day will surface any divergence" hedge; documents the actual two-call shape with sibling-context for Indeed (inline) vs LinkedIn (search-URL inline + get-JD deferred) vs Bing (both from get). **No `migration-required`** — internal adapter shape fix, no schema, env-var, config-file, or call-site change. Adapter remains opt-in-default-off; operators that enable `jobs-api14-bing` in `config/active_sources.txt` get functional rows on next triage cycle.

- **#778 fix(loose-ends): harness no longer hands rubric LLMs a truncated `dom_snippet` that hides the collection containers their hint metadata points at.** The cat-3 `empty_state_no_guidance` rubric is asked to judge whether a specific collection container is empty and unaccompanied by guidance, and its hint pipeline already supplies `collection_container_ids: ["rows"]` for board templates. But `dispatch_step` cut the DOM at a uniform `dom[:8000]`, and findajob's board templates render filter UI first (~28 KB) and the data `<tbody id="rows">` at the very bottom — so on `/board/dashboard?relevance_score_min=99` (29 KB total) the container the rubric was told to look at sat 21 KB past the truncation cliff. The 2026-05-21 v3 audit (`docs/personal/audit-reports/2026-05-21-walkthrough-run-v3/findings.jsonl`) caught the rubric returning `confidence: "high"` with a rationale that itself confessed "The DOM snippet is truncated and does not show the actual rendered content of the 'rows' collection container" — confident inference from button labels while admitting it couldn't observe. New top-level pure function `findajob.loose_ends.walkthrough.build_cat3_dom_snippet(dom, container_ids)`: keeps `dom[:8000]` as the page-top base (preserves the existing nav/header/buttons signal cat 3 reads alongside the container), then for each id in `collection_container_ids` appends `<!-- container: {id} -->\n<{tag} ...>{up to 4 KB}` located via `re.search` over `<(?:table|tbody|ul|ol|div)[^>]*\b(?:id|data-collection)="?<id>"?`. Cat 2's `flow_without_exit` call site stays on `dom[:8000]` deliberately — judges "is this an end state from page-top signals" which the first 8 KB already covers, and the issue body's three acceptance criteria are all cat-3-specific. Role prompt at `config/roles/loose_ends_empty_state_no_guidance.md` unchanged — it describes `dom_snippet` as "a redacted excerpt of the rendered DOM," generic enough that the additive assembly remains contract-compatible. Real-DOM verification on the failing audit's exact URL: 29 KB → 8,182-byte snippet that now contains `<tbody id="rows">` and the marker. Regression test (`test_build_cat3_dom_snippet_includes_container_past_truncation_boundary`) fixtures a synthetic ~30 KB DOM with `<tbody id="rows">` past byte 8000 and asserts the assembled snippet contains both the container element and its marker; three companion tests cover the additive page-top contract, missing-container defensive skip, and empty-container-ids → degrades to original `dom[:8000]` behavior. **No `migration-required`** — internal walkthrough-harness behavior, no schema, env-var, role-prompt, or call-site shape change.

### Changed

- **#823 feat(spend-ceiling): monthly LLM spend-ceiling now resets at the start of each calendar month in the stack's local timezone, not UTC.** Surfaced as polish item F8 during walk #2 of #672, deferred from #810/PR #820 because it's a code change not a doc fix. `findajob.cost_rollups.spend_this_month()` previously bucketed rows by `strftime('%Y-%m', logged_at) = strftime('%Y-%m', 'now')` — a UTC-only comparison that flipped a West-Coast operator's "this month" counter at 16:00 PT on the last day of the UTC month (mid-afternoon, the day before the operator's mental model). New implementation extracts a pure `_month_anchors_utc(tz, now_local)` helper mirroring `_week_anchors_utc`'s pattern (compute local-month-start, `astimezone(UTC)` to handle DST correctly, format as `"%Y-%m-%d %H:%M:%S"` matching `logged_at` storage) and switches the SQL filter from string-equality to a half-open range comparison. `spend_this_month(conn, tz=None, now=None)` reads `TZ` env when `tz` is omitted (default `"UTC"` — matches the codebase precedent at `findajob/web/routes/landing.py:42`).
