All three production callers — `spend_ceiling.check_call_gate`, `spend_ceiling.check_launch_gate`, `web/app.py:74` nav-chip — keep passing no override, inheriting the env default with no diff at the call sites. 9 new unit tests cover UTC, America/Los_Angeles (PDT and PST, including a March DST-transition row), Asia/Tokyo (UTC+9 ahead-of-UTC case), December→January year rollover, and boundary-row inclusion/exclusion between UTC and PT views of the same month. The cycle this change ships in has a one-time boundary anomaly: rows logged between the UTC month-start and the local month-start (up to 14h depending on offset) attribute differently before vs after the change — typically a one-time ~$0.50 effect, not operationally meaningful. `docs/getting-started/cost.md:104` updated to reflect TZ-aware semantics. **No `migration-required`** — behavior change in a helper function, no schema, env-var, or call-site shape change.

- **#768 ops(staging): `findajob-staging` joins the Watchtower auto-update set + poll cadence tightened to hourly.** The deployment host's existing Watchtower container already polled ghcr.io and auto-recreated the 5 tester stacks (alice/papa/dave/judy/tango); its `WATCHTOWER_POLL_INTERVAL` was tightened from `10800` (3h) to `3600` (1h) as part of this change so the staging soak gate picks up new digests within an hour instead of three. `findajob-staging` was explicitly opted out via `com.centurylinklabs.watchtower.enable=false` on its `scheduler` service, which meant the populated-soak pre-tag gate could test a stale `:latest` digest if the operator forgot to `docker compose pull` before running `python -m findajob.staging.green`. The lag surfaced during the #747 first verification pass (release-parity-matrix.md verification log, 2026-05-20: `/settings/excluded-employers/` returned 404 because the running image predated the same-day-merged #729). Resolution per Shape A in #768: remove the opt-out label from `scheduler` only on `/opt/stacks/findajob-staging/compose.yaml`. The `gmail-auth` setup-profile container (oneshot, not running steady-state) keeps its opt-out label. `findajob-clean` (NUX rehearsal stack) and the operator-primary-stack (operator's active stack) stay deliberately opted out — both have explicit rationales for operator-controlled cadence over auto-update. End-to-end verified post-change via `docker run --rm beatkind/watchtower:latest --run-once findajob-staging-scheduler-1`: scanned set went from 0 (when opted out) to 1 (now reachable); local-vs-remote SHA comparison returned `No pull needed. Skipping image.` — confirming the targeting works and the next digest advance will trigger a recreate. `docs/maintainers/release-parity-matrix.md` 2026-05-20 verification-log entry annotated with the closure marker. Per-stack opt-in/out status recorded in operator-private stack documentation. `ops/compose.yaml.example` unchanged — `enable=false` remains the safe default for new deployers, since unaffiliated users run their own Watchtower instance (or none at all) and should pick the cadence deliberately. **No `migration-required`** — operator-side single-stack opt-in flip; tracked example compose unchanged; unaffiliated deployers unaffected.

## [0.27.9] — 2026-05-22

### Fixed

- **#804 bug(detect-rejections): Tesla rejection emails surfaced in the review queue.** Tesla emails rejections from `noreply@tesla.com` (their own infrastructure, not a third-party ATS), and the default `rejection_sender_allowlist` only covered Greenhouse, Ashby, Lever, Workday, SmartRecruiters, Microsoft careers, and Oracle. Tesla emails were silently invisible to the detector — `SEARCH FROM "tesla.com"` was never issued, so the message wasn't fetched, classified, or surfaced in `/board/rejections-review/`. Added `tesla.com` to `DEFAULT_REJECTION_ALLOWLIST` in `findajob.gmail_imap` and to `SENDER_FINGERPRINTS` in `findajob.rejection_detector.patterns` (the parity test at `tests/test_gmail_imap_rejection_scan.py:68` enforces both surfaces stay in sync). New sanitized Tesla fixture under `tests/fixtures/rejection_emails/tesla/rejection.eml` is exercised by the layer1-high-confidence parametrize set, plus a focused regression test on the `FirstName Thank you for your interest in COMPANY` subject shape (distinct to Tesla's template, where the recipient's first name prefixes the subject line — `re.search` semantics make the leading token a non-issue, but pinning the behavior protects against future tightening of `_INTEREST_RE`). Companion `scripts/detect_rejections.py --since-days N` flag for one-shot historical rescan: bypasses the UID checkpoint and date-windows the IMAP search to the prior `N` days (capped at `_MAX_BACKLOG_WINDOW_DAYS=60`), emits a distinct `rejection_oneshot_rescan_started` event and `rejection_scan_completed{is_oneshot_rescan: true}` payload key, does not mutate `rejection_backlog_scan_complete`, and relies on the existing `new_uid > current` guard so historical UIDs don't roll the checkpoint backward. The `INSERT OR IGNORE` on `gmail_message_id` makes the operation safe to re-run. Documented in `docs/usage.md` § Rejection detection alongside the steady-state and first-run schedules. **No `migration-required`** — the allowlist's `persisted ∪ DEFAULT` floor (#658) means each stack picks up `tesla.com` on next config load, no schema or env-var changes.

## [0.27.8] — 2026-05-22

### Removed

- **#799 remove(feedback-widget): rip out the in-app feedback widget.** The floating "Feedback" button at the bottom-right of every page POSTed to `api.github.com/repos/{repo}/issues` via a `GITHUB_FEEDBACK_PAT` configured per-stack — a model that doesn't generalize beyond the operator's stacks. For an unaffiliated Fly.io deployer the widget rendered → click returned `503 "Feedback isn't configured on this stack."` with no documented fix path; the two routes to make it work (hosted gateway endpoint vs asking each deployer to mint their own PAT) both contradicted the "works without operator involvement" goal of the Fly.io Public Launch milestone. GitHub Issues + Discussions already exist as the primary feedback channels and are cited in `README.md` § "Privacy and contributing" and in `docs/getting-started/start-here-fly.md` § "Now what?". Removed code: `src/findajob/web/routes/feedback.py`, `src/findajob/web/templates/_feedback_widget.html`, `src/findajob/web/templates/_feedback_result.html`, `tests/test_web_feedback.py`; removed the `feedback` import + `include_router(feedback.router)` line in `src/findajob/web/routes/__init__.py`; removed the `{% include "_feedback_widget.html" %}` line from `src/findajob/web/templates/base.html`. Doc surfaces updated: `README.md` § "Privacy and contributing" bullet removed; `docs/getting-started/start-here-fly.md` "If you get stuck" line now points at GitHub Issues only; `docs/architecture/file-map.md` row removed; `docs/maintainers/release-parity-matrix.md` row + pass-4 narrative bullet removed. Historical `docs/roadmap.md` decision-log entry (referencing the prior #620 widget-500 bug) left intact as dated record. **`migration-required`** — operators with stacks already deployed should remove `GITHUB_FEEDBACK_PAT` and `FEEDBACK_STACK_LABEL` lines from each stack's state-volume `.env` (no longer read by anything in `findajob.*`); leaving them in place is harmless but stale.

### Changed

- **#805 docs(readme): surface JSearch alongside jobs-api14 in setup sections.** Documentation drift from #408 (curated RapidAPI feed picker, shipped 2026-04-09): the picker treats jobs-api14 and JSearch as peers (both written by the onboarding interview to `config/active_sources.txt`, both sharing `RAPIDAPI_KEY`), and `docs/getting-started/api-keys.md` + `docs/getting-started/install-docker.md` document them that way — but the README's §Pre-Deploy Requirements still listed only "RapidAPI (jobs-api14)" as if it were the sole option. New users hitting jobs-api14's 150 req/mo cap had no signpost to JSearch's 200 req/mo BASIC tier as an alternative. README §Pre-Deploy now names both with parallel quota framing and points at `/settings/active-sources/` for the flip; `docs/getting-started/configure.md`'s `## config/jsearch_queries.txt` section gains a one-paragraph activation note pointing at the same UI surface. README §Step 1 left unchanged: the generic "RapidAPI (optional)" already covers both adapters since they share a key. **No `migration-required`** — documentation only.

## [0.27.7] — 2026-05-22

### Added

- **#665 feat(web): nav-bar chip showing OpenRouter key's remaining credit.** Sibling to the existing spend chip; answers "when will I run out of credit?" rather than "am I spending too fast?". Reads `limit_remaining` directly from `GET /api/v1/auth/key` rather than computing `limit - usage` as the original issue body proposed — the API has a dedicated field, and for keys with periodic resets (`limit_reset='weekly'`/`monthly`) the `limit - usage` formula collapses because `usage` is lifetime cumulative while `limit` is per-period. New module `findajob.openrouter_credits` with 5-min in-process cache (single-worker uvicorn, restart resets); failure-open contract: missing key, blank key, HTTP 4xx/5xx, network failure, schema drift, and free-tier/no-limit keys (`limit_remaining=null`) all return `None` → template hides the chip silently. Threshold colors via `OPENROUTER_CREDIT_AMBER_USD` (default $5) and `OPENROUTER_CREDIT_RED_USD` (default $1). Per-stack: each stack queries its own `OPENROUTER_API_KEY` from `data/.env`. 15 unit tests + 5 integration tests through the real Jinja template render path — visual three-state confirmation via local uvicorn + Playwright at 1400px viewport. **No `migration-required`** — purely additive helper + template extension + Jinja global; no schema, config, cron, mount, or compose changes. No new dependencies — uses stdlib `urllib.request` matching `findajob.llm.openrouter`.

### Fixed

- **#753 fix(onboarding): forbid partial-character opaque-token reflections in the interviewer prompt.** Mid-interview the onboarding interviewer hallucinated `last 4 chars` substrings of just-provided opaque tokens (`ntfy_topic`, future API-key tails) — storage was correct but the chat reflection was wrong by one character. Tokenizer-level recall of arbitrary non-language strings is unreliable; the LLM invented the partial-character "verification" politeness pattern unprompted, since the prompt never instructed it. Fix is prompt-only: added a Phase-5 'Confirming opaque tokens' rule requiring full-value verbatim echo in code-fenced backticks with an explicit anti-pattern against `last N characters` / substring reflections, plus a local restatement at the `ntfy_topic.txt` section (the documented #672 failure site) so the rule fires on the actual emission path. Two new regression tests in `test_onboarding_role_prompt_invariants.py` assert both the positive rule and the anti-pattern are present in the general rule AND restated locally at the ntfy_topic.txt section — a soft contains-check on "verbatim" alone would pass against a docstring tweak that lost the actual rule. **No `migration-required`** — prompt + tests only.

### Changed

- **#755 feat(onboarding): defer greeting LLM call out of `/onboarding/interview/start`.** Pre-#755, `POST /onboarding/interview/start` ran a synchronous `run_turn()` inline to generate the initial assistant greeting before redirecting — measured ~25-28s p50 on a freshly-reset stack (curl 26.7s, Playwright requestSubmit 28.1s, Playwright click 25.0s — all against `findajob-clean` v0.27.2 with cold model), and the user saw a spinning Start button for the full duration before page transition. Now `/start` is a fast session-resolve + 303 (<1s); the kickoff turn is fired by the chat page's JS auto-fire handler against `/turn-stream` on load (same SSE plumbing as user turns, reusing `_stream_turn` / `handleFinish` / FILE-block badge rendering — no separate streaming path). Three advisor-flagged sharp edges handled: (1) server-side idempotency guard in `_stream_turn` — if `message == _KICKOFF_USER_MESSAGE && len(history) > 0`, the SSE error event carries `kind='kickoff_replay'` and the LLM is never called (race-safe via the session row as the lock for back/forward nav or two-tab concurrent fires); (2) `kind='kickoff_failed'` error discriminator for any error path when history is empty (length-finish, mid-stream error, TOCTOU spend-ceiling), with the underlying cause preserved as `original_kind` so the JS handler renders an explicit "Retry greeting" amber affordance instead of the generic red banner that says "keep typing to retry" (which doesn't apply when there's no greeting yet); (3) `kickoff_replay` JS path silently reloads (the server's GET handler renders the existing greeting from persisted history, so the user lands on the correct state without a confusing banner). The kickoff message stays server-authoritative: the `_KICKOFF_USER_MESSAGE` Python constant flows through `_render_chat`'s context into the template as `data-kickoff-message="Begin the interview."`, paired with `data-kickoff-pending="true"` rendered conditionally when history is empty — no JS-side copy of the constant that could drift. Walkthrough harness updated to match: post-`/start` redirect now lands in <1s instead of needing 120s defensive `wait_for_url`, so that budget drops to 30s, and an explicit `wait_for_selector("[data-role='assistant']", timeout=60_000)` between redirect-landing and turn-loop entry covers the streaming greeting's cold-model latency (the wait that used to live inside `/start` is now externalized). Five stale `/start` tests removed (`test_start_uses_tester_credentials`, `test_start_handles_runner_error`, `test_start_error_emits_log_event`, `test_start_writes_cost_log_row`, `test_start_clears_error_state_on_success_retry`) because their asserted semantics — LLM-call routing, in-route error handling, cost_log emission, error-state clear-on-retry — all moved to `/turn-stream` and are covered by the existing streaming-route test suite plus three new tests (`test_kickoff_replay_guard_refuses_when_history_non_empty`, `test_kickoff_failed_kind_on_length_finish_when_history_empty`, `test_kickoff_failed_kind_on_mid_stream_error_when_history_empty`) and one negative control (`test_post_kickoff_error_keeps_original_kind_when_history_non_empty`). Integration test (`test_full_interview_flow_writes_all_files_and_sentinel`) now simulates kickoff via `/turn` (same `urlopen` mock catches both transports) so the inject-pipeline assertions are unchanged. **No `migration-required`** — runtime behavior change is user-visible (snappier first-click NUX, no schema/config/cron/mount/compose surface touched); existing in-flight sessions continue to render correctly from persisted history regardless of which side of the upgrade they were created on.
- **#737 refactor(openrouter): centralize `openrouter_truncated` emission in the `complete()` wrapper.** Pre-#737 the same fix shape (raise `max_tokens` + emit `openrouter_truncated`) recurred three times — #639 (`fit_analyst`), #666 (`interview_prep`), #678 (`company_discoverer`) — because the emission lived in `findajob.llm.role_runner.run_role` and direct callers of `findajob.llm.openrouter.complete` got nothing. After #737 the wrapper itself emits `openrouter_truncated` whenever `finish_reason == "length"` on either branch (partial-truncation success path AND null-content + length failure path), so every direct `complete()` caller — current and future — inherits the diagnostic uniformly. Threaded an optional `job_id: str | None = None` kwarg through `complete()` so job-scoped callers (prep, interview_prep, fit_analyst) carry job context into the event payload; non-job callers (discoverer) pass `None`. `OpenRouterError` gains an optional `completion_tokens: int | None` attribute so the null-content branch can pass token-count through to the wrapper-level emitter. Removed the duplicate emissions in `role_runner.run_role` and `discoverer.runner.run`. **Consumer-visible `pipeline.jsonl` schema change:** `openrouter_truncated.completion_tokens` is now always `int` (was `null` on the discoverer's null-content branch pre-#737). Grafana / jq panels that filtered via `select(.completion_tokens != null)` will see new rows for the previously-null cases. The discriminator between partial truncation and hard truncation moves to `content_chars` (`> 0` = partial, `== 0` = null-content), which was already part of the payload — no migration needed for consumers that already read `content_chars`. **No `migration-required`** — code refactor with a backwards-compatible event-payload widening; existing consumers continue to work.
- **#787 docs(release-process): drop stale "writable Google Sheet" claim from pre-tag smoke prerequisites.** `scripts/test_container_integration.sh` has not depended on a Google Sheet since the form-ingest retirement (#62) — the script's prereqs are live API keys plus a candidate-profile fixture, no sheet read or write. `release-process.md` §"Pre-tag smoke check" still claimed "9 live API keys + a writable Google Sheet" in the deferred-CI-wiring paragraph; trimmed to match reality. No code change (script was already clean); pure docs trim. **No `migration-required`** — documentation only.

## [0.27.6] — 2026-05-21

### Added

- **#196 feat(web): /stats/throughput — per-ISO-week stacked-bar dashboard for applied/interview/offer transitions.** Flips the Throughput tab live in `templates/stats/_tabs.html`, ships the route + Jinja template + 8 unit tests. All-time view (no rolling window) — operator reads multi-month rhythm at a glance. Source is `audit_log` rows where `field_changed='stage'` AND `new_value IN ('applied','interview','offer')` so the dashboard measures *event throughput*, not currently-applied job count: a job that re-cycles applied→rejected→reactivated→applied contributes two applied ticks. Week label format `%Y-W##` from SQLite's `strftime('%Y-W%W', changed_at)`; `%W` is Monday-based and close-enough to ISO 8601 for at-a-glance cadence (strict ISO `%V` is not exposed by SQLite). Series colors `#059669/#10b981/#22c55e` match the late-funnel slice of `/stats/funnel`'s ramp so "applied = dark green" reads consistently across `/stats/*`. Empty-state guard renders informative copy ("No stage transitions to applied/interview/offer recorded yet") rather than an empty chart or 500. Negative-assertion test pins out-of-scope rows (`field_changed='user_notes'`, `new_value='scored'/'rejected'/'manual_review'`) excluded from the payload — protects against WHERE-clause regressions. Data-table row order is descending by week so recent activity reads at the top. **No `migration-required`** — purely additive route + template + tab flip + new tests; no schema, config, cron, mount, or compose changes.

## [0.27.5] — 2026-05-21

### Added

- **#195 feat(web): /stats/rejections — all-time rejection breakdown dashboard.** Final dashboard in the 14e stats arc; flips the Rejections tab live in `templates/stats/_tabs.html`, ships the route + Jinja template + 11 unit tests. Two cuts: (a) global per-`reject_reason` bar chart + data table over the canonical reason taxonomy (from `load_reject_reasons()` per #436), with legacy/free-text reasons appended after canonical; (b) per-company top-5 stacked bar chart + matrix table, segmented by reason. Sources from `jobs.stage IN ('rejected','not_selected')` so the view captures BOTH user rejections (also in `feedback_log`) AND company NOT_SELECTED events (which by design never reach `feedback_log` because they must not contaminate the scorer's feedback loop — this inclusion is the central distinction from `/stats/feedback`). Page subtitle explicitly links to `/stats/feedback` and explains the orthogonal cut: feedback is reason-axis × 28-day trend, rejections is reason-axis × company-axis × all-time. Stacked-bar choice for the per-company chart (rather than grouped) keeps the visual readable: 11 reasons × 5 companies grouped = 55 thin bars; stacked = 5 segmented bars. Color palette matches `/stats/feedback` so the same reason reads as the same hue across pages. **Amendment vs the issue's original AC, surfaced during pre-implementation drift audit (issue was 28 days old):** the issue body cited `stats.py:60-65` for the disabled-tab marker, which is stale (those lines now describe `SCORING_COLUMNS` after PR #773); the actual tab state lived in `_tabs.html`. The audit also identified that `/stats/feedback` (PR #200, 28 days ago) had shipped a partial rejection-reason view in the interim — the new page's value-add reframed as the per-company axis + all-time window + inclusion of NOT_SELECTED. **No `migration-required`** — purely additive route + template + tab flip + new tests; no schema, config, cron, mount, or compose changes.

### Changed

- **#775 chore(release): retire per-tester pin discipline; every stack tracks `:latest`.** Replaces the `:vMAJOR.MINOR` cohort-pin model with one uniform pin across every deploy surface (operator stacks, dogfood `findajob-clean`, soak tier `findajob-staging`, all five tester stacks, and Fly). Each release now reaches every stack in the same operational pass — a single `docker compose pull && docker compose up -d && python -m findajob.web.verify_auth` per stack with no per-tester `.env` edits and no per-release `ops/fly.toml.example` image-pin bump. The immutable `:vX.Y.Z` tags remain on GHCR as the audit trail and as the freeze target for anyone who specifically needs to pin. Templates ship `:latest` permanently: `ops/compose.yaml.example` defaults `FINDAJOB_IMAGE_TAG=latest`, `ops/fly.toml.example` image pin = `:latest`, `ops/stack.env.example` default = `latest`. `docs/maintainers/release-process.md` reframed accordingly: image-tag taxonomy table names `:latest` as the recommended pin, the three-gate dev pipeline (`clean` / `staging` / production) all track `:latest`, and the cohort-deploy section flows top-to-bottom without referencing the retired discipline. Sweeps doc-cruft across `docs/`, `ops/`, and root-level convention files per the lean-docs principle: removed historical version-narrative references (`since v0.X`, `pre-v0.Y`, "deployed before :v0.10.0", "Why no dogfood window"). Current behavior is described normatively; the git log carries the why. No `migration-required` — purely docs + config templates; existing stacks pulling `:latest` already pick up the new behavior with no action.

### Fixed

- **#780 fix(loose-ends): #751 — tune phase-2 audit (URL + parser + exclusion + itinerary).** Closes #751's four ACs: (AC1) `dashboard_all_filters_applied` walkthrough URL changed from `?col=__nonexistent__&col_min=99` (silently dropped by `findajob.web.filters` parser) to `?relevance_score_min=99` — recognized column with impossible threshold, produces the actual empty-state the rubric needs to evaluate. (AC2) Added one exclusion entry for `(established_user, /board/applied, flow_without_exit)`; the rubric correctly returns `is_loose_end=false` (nav affordances are present), and the operator's intuition concern is `action_without_confirmation`, a different rubric category tracked in #779. (AC3) Expanded the established_user itinerary from 5 → 8 walkthroughs (`not_selected_default_view`, `archive_default_view`, `materials_index_browse`) — three production surfaces that the original 5-walkthrough itinerary never exercised. (AC4) `rejected_view_with_data` flagged `is_loose_end=true` with operator agreement — `/board/rejected` empty state lacks "no rejections yet" guidance copy. Two adjacent fixes the audit surfaced: `_HintParser` now recognizes `<tbody id="...">` as a collection container (findajob's board templates carry the `id` on `<tbody id="rows">`, not the parent `<table>`; without this, the rubric received empty `collection_container_ids` for every board tab and couldn't evaluate empty-state loose ends), and `walk_loose_ends.py` picks basic-auth credentials per persona via `_resolve_creds` (`FINDAJOB_CLEAN_*` / `FINDAJOB_STAGING_*` / legacy `FINDAJOB_TEST_*` fallback).
