No `migration-required` — script + library tuning only.

## [0.27.4] — 2026-05-21

### Added

- **#194 feat(web): /stats/scoring — score-distribution histograms for the four score columns.** Flips the Scoring tab live in `templates/stats/_tabs.html`, ships the route + Jinja template + 6 unit tests. Renders one histogram per score column over the last 30 days: `relevance_score` and `interview_likelihood` (1-10 integer, 10 buckets — one per integer; written by the scorer on every job) plus `fit_score` and `probability_score` (0-100 float, 10 decile buckets `[0,10)…[90,100]`; written by prep Phase B only and NULL for the bulk of scored jobs). Per-chart subtitle surfaces non-NULL row count over total scored ("N of M scored jobs have a value") so sparse Phase B coverage is a visible signal rather than an empty chart. Bar charts via Chart.js, server-serialized payload in a `<script type="application/json">` anchor (no fetch-on-load); the rendered data table mirrors the chart for screen readers and noscript users. **Two amendments to the issue's original AC, surfaced during pre-implementation validation (issue was 28 days old):** (1) AC #1 said "three histograms" but a fourth scorer column (`interview_likelihood`) landed after the issue was filed and has full scorer coverage — shipped as a fourth chart rather than dropping a free signal. (2) AC #2 named `jobs.created_at` as the 30-day window predicate, which is ingest time, not score time — a job ingested 31+ days ago but scored today would be excluded, and an ingested-but-never-scored job would be included. Pivoted to `audit_log` on `field_changed='stage' AND new_value='scored'` within the window (the same query shape the funnel route uses), which matches AC #1's "scored jobs" intent. Both amendments are documented in the Session 2026-05-21 note on #194 for future-session context. Test fixture follows the established `test_web_stats_feedback.py` inline-schema pattern. **No `migration-required`** — purely additive route + template + tab flip + new tests; no schema, config, cron, mount, or compose changes.

- **#650 feat(web): /tools/ operator console — manual triggers for 7 cron jobs + pipeline.jsonl log viewer.** Promotes `/tools/` from a guided-prompt placeholder into a real operator surface. New `Run a job now` panel renders 7 trigger tiles — triage, detect-rejections, discover, notify-health, notify-stats, watchdog, notify-scoreboard (rendered disabled to mirror its yaml flag). Each tile shows the last-run timestamp from `pipeline.jsonl`, a `Running…` state while a matching cron is in flight, and an `Est. cost` row for the two LLM-spending crons (placeholder values for v1; real cost-estimate hookup is a follow-up). Cost-bearing triggers (`triage`, `discover`) require a browser `confirm()` prompt before POST. Triggers fire detached subprocesses through the new shared `findajob.web.cron_dispatch.dispatch_cron()` helper — same launch code path the `/board/trigger-triage` banner route (#752) now delegates to, so the banner's redirect destination is preserved while the gate semantics consolidate. The dispatcher enforces (in order): registry lookup (404 on unknown slug), enabled check (409 disabled), concurrency check via `is_currently_running()` JSONL scan (409 already-running with per-cron `max_runtime_minutes` ceiling so a leaked `cron_started` self-clears), spend-ceiling check via `check_launch_gate(db)` for gated crons (402 when over). Race-close: the dispatcher itself emits `cron_started` immediately before `subprocess.Popen` so a follow-up POST during the ~100ms child-interpreter startup window correctly sees the run as already-running. New `/tools/logs/pipeline/` reads via `findajob.admin.jsonl_tail.tail_events()` and renders the last 200 events with a single-select event-name filter (typeahead dropdown sourced from observed event names in the window). v1 explicitly excludes severity filter / time-range filter / 5s auto-refresh / gzipped-rotation traversal — each becomes a follow-up issue. Observability win independent of #650: new `findajob.audit.cron_event_span(name)` context manager wraps `main()` in `triage.py`, `notify.py`, `discover_companies.py`, `watchdog.py`, `detect_rejections.py` so every cron run emits paired `cron_started` + `cron_finished` events (with `status='succeeded'|'failed'`) regardless of script implementation. The concurrency gate + log viewer + future `/tools/` widgets all read the same source. **Disclosed verification gap** per `feedback_disclose_verify_gaps`: integration tests cover all dispatch branches and the log viewer with synthetic JSONL fixtures, but the canonical verification (each of the 7 buttons clicked through on findajob-clean post-merge, with the log viewer cross-checking event arrival in real time) is **non-negotiable post-merge** and must complete before considering the feature shipped. **No `migration-required`** — purely additive routes + helpers + new tests; no schema, config, cron schedule, or mount changes.

- **#729 feat(settings): /settings/excluded-employers/ — structured editor for the deterministic exclusion list.** Pre-#729 operators edited `config/excluded_employers.yaml` via `/config/`'s raw text editor with no validation feedback — a regex typo would surface only at the next pipeline run. New `/settings/excluded-employers/` page renders two visually-separated sections (Exact + Regex) with Alpine.js add/remove affordances and HTMX partial-swap for the save result. Loader (`load_excluded_employers`) switched from module-cached to read-per-call so saves take effect on the next request without container restart, consistent with the other config-aware settings pages (active-sources, reject-reasons, connections, gmail-config). No `migration-required` — purely additive route + template; the YAML file already existed.

- **#8 feat(audit): in-process rotation for `logs/pipeline.jsonl`.** The file caps at 5 MB; on threshold cross, the current file is gzipped to `pipeline.jsonl.1.gz`, older `.gz` backups shift up (`.1.gz` → `.2.gz`, …), and the ring keeps the 6 most recent. Any backup older than 90 days is also swept at the end of every rotation regardless of slot. Total disk footprint per stack is now bounded at a few MB instead of growing unbounded (operator's stack was at 4.99 MB after 36 days pre-#8 across 8 cohort stacks). Implemented inline in `src/findajob/audit.py` rather than via `logging.handlers.RotatingFileHandler` — three of the four needed features (gzip on rotation, 90-day mtime sweep, monkeypatch-friendly `LOG_PATH` resolution for tests) require custom hooks anyway, and stdlib's per-process open file handle would have introduced a multi-process race the existing open-append-close pattern avoids. The hot path stays open-append-close (POSIX `O_APPEND` writes ≤ PIPE_BUF are atomic, so no lock is needed there); the rare rotation block is serialized across the supercronic+uvicorn processes with a non-blocking `fcntl.flock` on a sidecar `<path>.rotate.lock` file. If another process is mid-rotation, the would-be caller skips silently and the next call retries. Reader compat: `findajob.admin.jsonl_tail` already reads only the trailing 1 MB so the admin dashboard is unaffected; `findajob.staging.green._read_events` extended to also read `pipeline.jsonl.1.gz` so the 26h `pipeline_complete` predicate survives a rotation that lands between green-check runs. Docs in `docs/operations/README.md` replace the prior manual-`logrotate` workaround. No `migration-required` — purely additive runtime behavior, no schema/config/compose change.

- **#752 feat(dashboard): first-triage empty-state banner with one-click trigger.** Eliminates the "No matches." cliff a fresh-onboarded user lands on between completing onboarding and the first cron-triggered triage cycle. New `_first_triage_banner.html` partial renders above the (empty) job table when three conditions hold: `jobs` table count == 0, `data/.onboarding-complete` sentinel mtime < 48h ago, and the `first_triage_banner_dismissed` cookie is unset. Banner copy includes the next scheduled triage time (TZ-aware, sourced from `ops/scheduled-jobs.yaml` with `FINDAJOB_TRIAGE_SCHEDULE` env-var override), addresses the common discoveries-vs-jobs question ("Discoveries above are research targets only; scored jobs arrive after triage runs"), and surfaces a **Trigger triage now** button that POSTs to a new `/board/trigger-triage` route. The route gates on the existing monthly LLM spend ceiling (402 with refusal copy when reached), spawns `scripts/triage.py` as a detached subprocess, emits a single `web_cron_dispatched` event (with `cron=triage`, `source=dashboard_banner`) to `pipeline.jsonl` (subsequent `pipeline_started` → `pipeline_complete` events come from triage.py itself; no double-emission), and 303s back to `/board/dashboard?triage_launched=1` where the banner swaps to a confirmation state ("Triage started. Refresh in a few minutes…"). Banner self-suppresses once the jobs table has any rows — no client-side polling needed. Cookie-dismiss via `?dismiss_first_triage_banner=1` for users who prefer to wait for the cron cycle. **Documentation:** `install-fly.md` §7 rewritten to lead with the dashboard banner + button as the primary affordance; the prior `fly ssh console --command python3 /app/scripts/triage.py` line moves to a power-user `<details>` block. **Trade-off documented:** V1 has no server-side idempotency tracking of manual-triage runs — the cron-vs-manual race at midnight stack-time is possible (cost ~$1-3 in the rare case), and a back-button-then-resubmit double-fire is possible (same cost). The monthly spend ceiling bounds the worst case. Follow-up: sentinel-file or `background_tasks` kind tracking for a deterministic "triage already in flight, refusing" response. **No `migration-required`** — purely additive route + template + state helper.

### Fixed

- **#770 + #771 fix(paths): introduce `IMAGE_ROOT` so Fly's split substrate (code at `/app/`, state at `/app/state/`) stops breaking docs + every web-spawned subprocess.** Surfaced during #747's Fly parity verification: `POST /board/jobs/{fp}/prep` on Fly 200'd, audit-logged `prep_in_progress`, then died — no `prep_started`, no `cost_log`, jobs stuck until watchdog reaped at 60min. Same root cause behind #770's `/docs/{slug}` 404. `findajob.paths.BASE` was being used for BOTH code-path resolution (e.g. `f"{BASE}/scripts/prep_application.py"`) AND state-path resolution (`f"{BASE}/data/pipeline.db"`). On Docker that worked because `JSP_BASE=/app` so BASE-as-code-root and BASE-as-state-root coincide. On Fly, `JSP_BASE=/app/state` (single-volume layout per `ops/fly.toml`), so `f"{BASE}/scripts/...` resolves to `/app/state/scripts/` — a directory that has never existed. `subprocess.Popen` returns a Popen object whether the exec target exists or not; the exec'd process fails immediately with `FileNotFoundError` and the route's try/except (which only catches Popen-construction failures) never sees it. Silent. Same shape on the docs route: `app.state.base_root / "docs"` resolved to `/app/state/docs/` → 404 across all 9 allowlisted slugs. New `findajob.paths.IMAGE_ROOT` constant is computed from `__file__` (`src/findajob/paths.py → /app` in the image) BEFORE any env override — load-bearing property. `BASE` retains its current state-root semantics (defaults to `IMAGE_ROOT`, overridden by `JSP_BASE`). Every `f"{BASE}/scripts/..."` and `Path(BASE) / "scripts" / ...` call site switches to `IMAGE_ROOT` — 13 launch sites across `src/findajob/{actions,fetchers/__init__,notifications/feedback_review,discoverer/runner,prep/orchestrator,web/routes/board_actions,web/routes/speculative,web/cron_dispatch}.py` and `scripts/{ingest_form,manual_prep,backfill_jd}.py`. `findajob.web.app.create_app` accepts a new `image_root: Path | None = None` parameter alongside `base_root`, default `Path(IMAGE_ROOT)`; `app.state.image_root` is the route-side handle. `routes/docs.py` reads `image_root` instead of `base_root` for the docs-route `Path` lookup. Three shapes were considered (Shape A new `IMAGE_ROOT`; Shape B invert BASE = `__file__`-derived + add `STATE_ROOT`; Shape C entrypoint symlinks); Shape A picked because it's additive (~12 line edits + 1 new constant), self-documenting (variable names map directly to "where this lives"), and leaves the 175 existing state-path `BASE/...` usages untouched. Shape B would have required auditing every BASE reference; Shape C would have spread the substrate-divergence handling across code + entrypoint + fly.toml without anchoring the invariant in code. Regression-fence test in `tests/test_paths_image_root.py` spawns a subprocess with `JSP_BASE=/tmp/...` and asserts `IMAGE_ROOT != BASE` + `IMAGE_ROOT` doesn't drift to the env override (avoids the `feedback_reimport_invalidates_closures` trap by running the import in a fresh interpreter). `test_web_docs.py` fixtures updated to pass `image_root=tmp_path` so the docs route reads from the same fake root the test seeds. **Disclosed verification gap** per `feedback_disclose_verify_gaps`: 3005 unit tests pass + paths.py invariant pinned by subprocess test, but the canonical Fly verification per #771's acceptance — `POST /board/jobs/{fp}/prep` producing `prep_started` + `cost_log` entries; `POST /board/trigger-triage` producing `pipeline_started`; all 9 `/docs/{slug}` returning 200 against the live `:latest` on Fly — is non-negotiable post-merge before declaring done. **No `migration-required`** — purely additive constant + new optional `create_app` param + call-site swaps; no schema, config, cron, mount, or compose change.

- **#619 fix(web): HTMX-aware onboarding guard returns `HX-Redirect` for `HX-Request`-marked GETs to gated endpoints.** Defense-in-depth follow-up to #618 — the acute redirect-loop bug is already prevented two layers up (template-side gate on the bell `<li>` + ungated pages not rendering any badge HTML at all), but both of those defenses sit at the call-site / template layer and are easy to forget the next time a developer adds a nav widget that polls a guarded endpoint. New branch in `require_onboarding_complete` in `src/findajob/web/onboarding_guard.py`: when the guard fires AND the request carries `HX-Request: true`, raise `HTTPException(status_code=200, headers={"HX-Redirect": "/onboarding/"})` instead of the standard 307 + Location. HTMX honors `HX-Redirect` by setting `window.location` before any element swap, so the body content is never rendered into the trigger element — sidestepping the HTMX-follows-30x-and-swaps-redirect-body-into-element bug class entirely. Picked Option B (guard-level) over Option A (empty-200 specifically for `/notifications/badge`) because Option A would have been per-endpoint and per-future-widget; Option B is the only option that enforces the invariant at the boundary, where future nav widgets can't accidentally regress. The #618 template-side gate is preserved as the primary defense; this is belt-and-suspenders. Non-HTMX requests are unchanged (still 307 → `/onboarding/`). Tests in `tests/test_web_onboarding_guard.py` parametrize over `/notifications/badge`, `/board/dashboard`, and `/stats/funnel` with and without `HX-Request` to assert both halves of the contract on the same boundary — a future guarded endpoint added without thought still gets the right behavior. No `migration-required` — purely additive header behavior, no schema/config/cron/mount changes.

- **#738 fix(prep): Phase B emits per-step ntfy progress + materials page distinguishes Phase B from Phase A regen.** Operator reported clicking "Continue prep" on `/materials/{fp}/` and perceiving it as "only generated the briefing again." Production `pipeline.jsonl` evidence proved Phase A did NOT re-run (one `prep_phase_a_complete` at 12:12 UTC, `web_continue_prep_dispatched_from_materials` at 14:11 UTC, then `resume_quality_check` + `find_contacts` + `prep_complete` in the Phase B window with no second Phase A) — a UX bug, not a code regression. Root cause: Phase B fired exactly one ntfy notification (terminal `Drafts ready: ...`) and ran silently for the ~2–5 minute resume → changes → cover → critique → outreach span; the only stale notif on the operator's phone during that span was Phase A's earlier `Briefing ready: ...`. Compounding it, the materials page rendered `⟳ Regenerating…` for `stage='prep_in_progress'` — the same label a Phase A regenerate shows. New helper `_emit_phase_b_progress(outdir, step, label, action)` in `src/findajob/prep/orchestrator.py` writes a `.phase_b_step` sidecar (`"{n}/5 {label}\n"`) and fires `quick_notify("Phase B: {action}")` before each of the five visible LLM/subprocess steps — `1/5 resume` → `Tailoring resume…`, `2/5 changes` → `Reviewing resume changes…`, `3/5 cover` → `Drafting cover letter…`, `4/5 critique` → `Running recruiter critique…`, `5/5 outreach` → `Drafting outreach…`. The terminal `Drafts ready: ...` notif fires once after all five, unchanged. The materials route `folder_view` reads the sidecar only when `stage == 'prep_in_progress'` and passes it as `phase_b_step` to the template; `folder.html` renders `⟳ Phase B in progress — step N/5: <human-readable label>` with a step→label map (resume/changes/cover/critique/outreach → tailoring/reviewing/drafting/recruiter/drafting). The generic `⟳ Regenerating…` label still renders as the fallback when the sidecar is absent — preserves the Phase A regen path (legacy `--phase=all` route) and any future cold-start. Sidecar reads are gated on stage so a stale sidecar from a prior run can't bleed Phase B labeling into other stages. Drive-by cleanup in `_handle_phase_b_failure`: pre-#738 the failure path contained two consecutive duplicate `quick_notify` calls (a copy-paste), double-pinging the operator on every Phase B failure; reduced to single fire. Phase B also clears any stale `.phase_b_step` sidecar at entry (after the `outdir` validity check, before Stage 4) so a retry of a previously-failed Phase B doesn't briefly show the failed run's step label during the ~2–5 sec subprocess startup before the first new step writes the sidecar — advisor catch at pre-commit review. **Discriminator choice (deviation from issue body):** AC #2 implied audit-log inspection (prior `briefing_ready → prep_in_progress` transition) as the discriminator between Phase B and the legacy `--phase=all` regen path. This PR uses sidecar-presence instead — simpler, no DB read inside `folder_view`. Side effect: a `--phase=all` regenerate (Phase A → Phase B in one subprocess) will swap the materials-page label from `⟳ Regenerating…` to `⟳ Phase B in progress — step N/5: ...` once the orchestrator crosses into Phase B and writes the sidecar. Arguably better than the issue body proposed (more informative than a generic spinner that never changes), but it IS a deviation; surfaced here so future readers don't think it was an oversight. AC #4 (no stale Phase A messaging after Phase B) was already structurally guaranteed by `is_briefing_gate = stage == "briefing_ready"` in `folder_view` — the gate aside automatically hides on the `briefing_ready` → `prep_in_progress` transition that `/materials/{fp}/continue-prep` makes before spawning the subprocess. Tests: 4 in `tests/test_prep_phase_b_progress.py` (per-step notify order + sidecar advancement + failure-path stage reset + duplicate-fire regression) and 4 in `tests/test_materials_phase_b_progress.py` (sidecar-present label render + step→label map across all 5 keys + generic-fallback when absent + stage-gating). **Disclosed verification gap** per `feedback_disclose_verify_gaps`: end-to-end ntfy delivery is tested via the `quick_notify` spy (proves Phase B's call sequence), not via real ntfy delivery to a real phone. Browser-side verification of the materials-page label render is also not in this PR — the template branch is unit-tested, but the live look during a real Phase B run is the canonical verification and is non-negotiable post-merge on the operator's stack. **No `migration-required`** — purely additive helper + template branch + new tests; no schema, config, cron, or mount changes.

- **#743 fix(onboarding): SSE streaming now actually aborts on client disconnect.** Before #743, `complete_stream()`'s `try/finally` cleanup ran on client disconnect (no socket leak), but the upstream OpenRouter call kept reading urllib bytes until `[DONE]` — then wrote `cost_log`, `append_turn` × 2, and `update_captured_blocks`. Operator paid ~$0.05/cancelled turn (~$0.12 on a 3700-token Haiku response) and the cancelled assistant text showed up in chat history on next page load. Root cause: `complete_stream()` is a sync generator iterating urllib's blocking-read protocol; asyncio cancellation has no yield point to land on between SSE line reads, so any peek-based watcher loses the receive-channel race against Starlette's `listen_for_disconnect`. The reverted attempt in commit `228a6ef` (revert `fc6034c`) used a `threading.Event` + asyncio watcher polling `request.is_disconnected()` every 250ms — proven non-functional by browser smoke on findajob-clean (0/2 runs fired `stream_cancelled`; 94s and 99s server-side runtimes after 4–5s curl disconnects, $0.17 of OpenRouter spend during failed verification). New architecture: ASGI middleware in `src/findajob/web/middleware/disconnect_state.py` wraps `receive()` and records `http.disconnect` into `scope["findajob.client_disconnected"]` BEFORE any inner consumer (Starlette's listener, the SSE route, anything else) can observe it. The middleware is passively in the call chain — no race by construction. `complete_stream()` re-acquires the optional `is_cancelled: Callable[[], bool] | None` parameter from `228a6ef`'s function-level contract (which was correct in isolation — only the route-side cancellation signal source changes). The SSE route's `post_turn_stream` stays sync (no async-conversion needed) and passes a closure `lambda: scope.get(SCOPE_KEY, False)` as the callback. Cancellation polling happens once per `raw_line_bytes` iteration inside `complete_stream`'s SSE-read loop; on True it calls `resp.close()` and returns WITHOUT yielding `StreamFinish`. Absence of `StreamFinish` is the route's signal to skip persistence — `cost_log`, `append_turn`, and `update_captured_blocks` already lived inside the `finish` branch and never execute when the early return short-circuits the for-loop. A `stream_cancelled` event fires from `_stream_turn`'s `finally` (route="turn-stream", reason="client_disconnect", session_id=…) when the loop exits without a terminal chunk AND the callback confirms cancellation was the cause — distinguishing it from a hypothetical unexpected exception. **Polling cadence is gated by OpenRouter chunk arrival**: between line reads the sync generator is blocked on socket.recv(); if OpenRouter goes quiet for several seconds the flag is set but unpolled until the next chunk. Still ≪ the 50–90s the bug costs today (whole-response runtime). Test surface follows the advisor's "stub the LLM source, not `complete_stream`" prescription: 5 middleware unit tests in `tests/test_disconnect_state_middleware.py`, 3 new `complete_stream` cancellation tests in `tests/test_openrouter_stream.py`, and 2 end-to-end ASGI-direct-invocation tests in `tests/test_onboarding_interview_stream_disconnect.py` (urllib stubbed slow + production middleware + route + closure all real). **Disclosed verification gap** per `feedback_disclose_verify_gaps`: integration tests drive the ASGI app via `asyncio.run`, NOT a real uvicorn process. They confirm the middleware-flag-closure-callback chain works when `http.disconnect` IS delivered; they do NOT prove uvicorn (in production) actually delivers `http.disconnect` on a real client abort. **Browser smoke against the new `:latest` on findajob-clean is the canonical verification** for that final link and is non-negotiable before declaring done. **No `migration-required`** — purely additive middleware + LLM-module parameter + new tests; no schema, config, cron, or mount changes.

- **#661 fix(web): `/board/rejections-review/` reattribute affordance is usable.** The Reattribute form previously asked the operator to paste `jobs.id` — a UUID never surfaced in any board view, URL, or `data-` attribute. The freeform `<input type="text">` is replaced by a `<select>` populated from `jobs WHERE stage IN ('applied','interview','offer') AND synthetic = 0`, sorted `stage_updated DESC NULLS LAST, created_at DESC`. Each option renders as `{title} at {company} ({stage})`. When zero legal targets exist the form renders a non-actionable hint rather than an empty select. POST handler is unchanged — same `job_id` form field, same `('applied','interview','offer')` 409 guard as defense-in-depth. **Out of scope by design:** picking an already-archived row (`not_selected`/`withdrew`/`rejected`) as a reattribute target — the dropdown can't surface those; production signal showed every historical ambiguous suggestion was resolved via `dismiss`, with zero attempted reattribute outcomes. Revisit if cohort signal shifts. No `migration-required` — purely template + view-model addition. **Scope re-shaped during pre-implementation validation** from the issue's original Option B (per-ambiguous same-company candidate list) to the simpler dropdown after production data showed the headline CyrusOne case had two indistinguishable candidates (same title, both archived) and the operator's resolution for that case was already `dismiss`.

- **#735 fix(loose-ends): phase-2 `--output-dir` controls report location.** `write_report()` in `scripts/walk_loose_ends.py` was hardcoded to `docs/personal/audit-reports/` while `findings.jsonl` honored the CLI's `--output-dir`. Two same-day runs against different `--output-dir`s would isolate findings but clobber each other's reports. Pass the CLI argument through; drop the dead alias. No `migration-required` — script-only change.

## [0.27.3] — 2026-05-20

### Migration required

- **#498 `jobs.score_status` CHECK constraint tightened — `needs_info` dropped.** Pre-#498 the constraint permitted `'scored'`, `'manual_review'`, and `'needs_info'`; the third value was dead — never written by any code path, absent from `config/scoring_schema.json`, and verified zero rows across every active cohort stack at filing time. New `findajob.db.migrate._tighten_score_status_check_if_needed()` runs on every `apply_pending` and rebuilds the `jobs` table via the rename-create-copy-drop pattern when the live CHECK still includes `'needs_info'`. Pre-rebuild row-count guard: if any row carries `score_status='needs_info'`, the helper raises `RuntimeError` with a specific recovery message rather than letting `_rebuild_table_with_indexes` surface a buried CHECK violation; the legacy row is left untouched and the stack stops taking writes until cleaned (`UPDATE jobs SET score_status='scored' WHERE …` or operator-chosen value). Helper runs FIRST in `apply_pending`'s post-migration step (before `_add_briefing_ready_stage_if_needed` and `_add_prep_phase_b_kind_if_needed`) so its specific message wins over the generic one a sibling rebuild would surface. Idempotent — short-circuits when `'needs_info'` is no longer in the live schema. Fresh installs pick up the tightened constraint directly from the edited `0001_initial.sql:60`; existing stacks at `_meta.schema_version=1` absorb it on their next entrypoint run with no schema_version bump and no operator action.

### Removed

- **`indeed_title_allow:` per-stack post-filter retired (#417 → reversed).** The `JobsApi14IndeedAdapter` no longer post-filters titles against an inclusion regex. The infrastructure shipped in #417 (loader `load_indeed_title_allow_rules()`, adapter call, four field-specific example templates in `prefilter_rules.yaml.example`, doc note in `api-keys.md`, test class `TestLoadIndeedTitleAllowRules`) is deleted. Off-target Indeed rows now flow through the standard downstream layers — prefilter `hard_rejects:`, LLM scoring, and the rejection-tag feedback loop — same as every other adapter. Consolidates the invariant: feed-quality filtering happens at the prefilter/scorer layer, not per-adapter. Stacks with `indeed_title_allow:` configured in their `config/prefilter_rules.yaml` can leave the key in place (silently ignored); no migration action required. Engineering rationale: adding a per-adapter, per-stack-tunable knob to compensate for upstream-API deficits was duplicative of layers already present and required onboarding-time field-aware synthesis that was never implemented.

### Documentation

- **#673 README §Quick start: fork the Deploy section into Fly-first + Docker-self-host paths.** Before this change, the README §Deploy was 30+ lines of `docker compose up -d` framing with a single blockquote callout pointing at Fly. After: §Quick start opens with a two-path framing (Fly hosted = recommended for most; Docker self-host = for operators), each gets its own equal-weight §Deploy subsection, and §First-run onboarding is rewritten to be substrate-neutral (the gate sequence is identical on both paths). Onboarding sequence in the README now reflects the actual 5-step gate chain: Step 1 keys → Step 2 interview → spend-ceiling → Gmail → Connections. Interview cost claim updated to "~$1.50–$3" (matches live walkthrough measurement at $1.50; older "$3–6" was conservative). Adds the manual-trigger reference so users with empty dashboards know the affordance exists. Surfaced and validated during the unaffiliated-tester live walkthrough (#672, L1).

- **#672 live walkthrough — `install-fly.md` §7 triage runtime claim corrected.** Was "5–15 minutes the first time"; live measurement on a 20+-target-company profile ran 46 minutes (1,412 jobs ingested across greenhouse / linkedin / ashby). Rewrote to "5–60 minutes" with explanation that runtime scales with the number of target companies in the profile, and noted that subsequent daily runs are delta-only at 1–5 min. Surfaced as L13 in the live walkthrough log.

- **#672 live walkthrough — `install-fly.md` Step 1 + Step 4 honesty edits.** Step 1 now inlines the three per-OS flyctl install commands (`brew install flyctl` / `curl … fly.io/install.sh` / PowerShell `iex`) so a non-developer doesn't have to leave the runbook to discover the right command, with the Fly install page kept as a fallback. Step 4's "Creates the Fly app (asks before consuming the name)" parenthetical was inaccurate — `fly-deploy.sh` calls `fly apps create $APP` non-interactively, so a typo in `fly.toml`'s `app =` line consumes the wrong slug. Rewrote that line to spell out the no-confirmation behavior and how to recover (`fly apps destroy`). Surfaced during the unaffiliated-tester live walkthrough (#672); see L3/L4 in the local walkthrough log.

- **#672 live walkthrough — Fly template pin two minors stale.** `ops/fly.toml.example` was pinned to `:v0.25.0`, two minor releases behind current. A new user following `install-fly.md` step 3 ("Don't change anything else in `fly.toml` for a first deploy") would deploy code predating onboarding env-key detection (#676), RapidAPI live smoke (#689), the briefing-first prep gate (#691), the board UX surge (#696–#702), the Indeed allowlist retirement (#746), and SSE streaming (#740). Bumped to `:v0.27.2`. Root cause: `docs/maintainers/release-process.md` had no step covering the Fly template; a new bullet now makes it part of every release. Surfaced during the unaffiliated-tester live walkthrough (#672).

- **#672 dry-run doc cleanup.** `docs/getting-started/install-fly.md` "Time to value" framing rewritten to honestly state ~2 hours total to a populated dashboard (~20 min deploy + 60–90 min interview, with $10 OpenRouter top-up reminder for the ~$3–6 interview cost), instead of leading with "~20 minutes" and burying the interview duration as a parenthetical. Three broken doc links repaired: `docs/getting-started/install-docker.md` (3 occurrences of `../release-process.md` corrected to `../maintainers/release-process.md`) and `docs/getting-started/README.md` §6 (`restore.md` corrected to `../operations/restore.md`). Surfaced during the unaffiliated-tester walkthrough pre-flight (#672 dry-run, 2026-05-19).

## [0.27.2] — 2026-05-19

### Added

- **#740 feat(onboarding): SSE streaming for partial FILE-block emissions in the chat UI.** New `findajob.llm.openrouter.complete_stream()` generator yields typed chunks (`captured` / `finish` / `error`) progressively as OpenRouter emits SSE events. New `POST /onboarding/interview/turn-stream` route drives the generator and re-emits SSE events to the browser; each `<<<END FILE: name>>>` close marker triggers a "📄 captured" chip in the chat UI as it arrives, rather than the operator waiting silently for 60-180s on the full turn. Frontend consumer is a vanilla-JS IIFE in `src/findajob/web/static/onboarding-stream.js` (fetch + ReadableStream, no new deps). The non-streaming `/turn` route remains as the documented fallback for no-JS / test environments (AC#7's "or for test environments" branch); production traffic flows through the streaming endpoint via `interview.html`'s `data-stream-endpoint` form attribute. Retry boundary is by yield-state — pre-first-yield retries `{rate_limit, upstream, network}` × 3 with the same exponential backoff `complete()` uses; post-first-yield surfaces failure as an in-band SSE `error` event with no retries. Spend-ceiling gate runs synchronously before the SSE response opens — `LLMSpendCeilingExceeded` returns a 402 JSON response, not an SSE error event; a defensive guard inside the generator catches the TOCTOU window between gate and stream open. Response includes `X-Accel-Buffering: no` so buffering reverse proxies (Fly's edge, generic nginx-fronted deploys, etc.) don't hold the chunks back. Cost-log + `append_turn` + `update_captured_blocks` fire on the `finish` event with the same shape the `/turn` route writes today (`operation="onboarding_interviewer"`, override fields, `clear_error` on success). `finish_reason="length"` translates to an SSE error event (`kind="length"`) without persisting the turn — exact parity with the existing route's pre-persistence raise. Test surface: 10 new tests in `tests/test_openrouter_stream.py` against a real captured OpenRouter SSE response (`tests/fixtures/llm/openrouter_sse_haiku_streaming.txt`, captured live during the design-time urllib spike that confirmed `urllib.request.urlopen + resp.readline()` streams incrementally — TTF 1.19s, span 3.06s across 268 lines), 11 route tests in `tests/test_onboarding_interview_stream_route.py`, plus the existing 25 `/turn` route tests continue to exercise the persistence-regression bed via the fallback path. **No `migration-required`** — purely additive route + JS asset + LLM-module function; no schema, config, cron, or mount changes.

- **feat(loose-ends): #572 — static UX loose-end audit Phase 1.** New `scripts/audit_loose_ends.py` script and `findajob.loose_ends/` package walk the source tree, diff user-input-file consumers against UI-surface coverage, and emit a dated markdown report. Operator-curated `config/audit_exclusions.yaml` (tracked) carries the intentional-CLI-only allowlist. Two LLM calls per run (classifier at `temperature=0` for cross-run determinism; prose-writer at default). Quarterly manual trigger; ≤ $0.50/run budget self-enforced by the shim (exit 2 on overrun). Spec: `docs/superpowers/specs/2026-05-18-572-ux-audit-phase1-design.md`.

- **(#572 Phase 2) Dynamic UX walkthrough** — Playwright-driven loose-end audit covering categories 2 (flows-without-exit) and 3 (empty-states-without-guidance). Two personas (`nux_user` @ `findajob-clean`, `established_user` @ `findajob-staging`), YAML-driven itinerary, per-page LLM evaluator at temperature=0. Hard cost ceiling $2.00/run. Phase 1 (static, #730) and Phase 2 close the original #572 issue together.

### Changed

- `_job_row.html` now emits `data-stage="{{ row.stage }}"` on each `<tr>` (additive attribute). Enables structural selectors for the #572 Phase 2 walker; no rendering change. Pre-existing `data-fingerprint` attribute remains.

- **#726 refactor(actions): `un_apply_job` + `reactivate_from_ingest` gain `deferred_fs` parity with #709.** The two remaining helpers in `findajob.actions` that carried the same fs-then-DB ordering #709 removed from the other seven. Not bug-triggering today (no composing callers), but eliminates the inconsistency while the pattern is still fresh. `un_apply_job` intentionally collapses its folder-move + per-snapshot deletes into one closure whose body iterates `glob("*.md")` at execution time — different shape from #709's `un_not_selected_job` (N closures, each binding one `marker_path`); both are valid. New regression test `test_un_apply_job_multiple_snapshots_single_closure_no_capture_trap` seeds 2 snapshot files and asserts both are deleted on execute, locking in the single-closure shape. **No `migration-required`** — pure refactor, no schema/config/cron/mount changes.

### Fixed

- **#740 fix(onboarding): hotfix — `hx-boost='false'` on the streaming form.** Follow-up to PR #741 (#742). The streaming chat form was being intercepted by HTMX's global boost behavior, breaking the SSE stream attachment in the browser. Setting `hx-boost='false'` on the form element opts out of boost for that specific control, letting the vanilla-JS SSE consumer attach to the response stream as designed. Lands same-day as #741. **No `migration-required`** — template attribute change only.

- **#739 fix(prep): cover letter `.docx` heading + paragraph spacing regressions.** Two coordinated fixes against the cover-letter render path. (1) **Heading template** — `config/roles/cover_letter_writer.md:66` previously instructed the LLM to emit `# Cover Letter | {Company} | {Job Title}`; the redundant "Cover Letter |" prefix is gone, the heading now reads `# {Company} | {Job Title}`. Takes effect on the next cover letter generated after deploy. (2) **Paragraph spacing** — `_add_cover_letter_spacing` in `src/findajob/prep/docx_postprocess.py` was supposed to apply `Pt(12)` `space_after` to every body paragraph (the `BodyText` style in `config/reference.docx` has `w:after="20"` ~1pt, which renders too tight). But its `from docx import Document` was inside the function's bare `try / except Exception: pass` block, AND `python-docx` was missing from `pyproject.toml` dependencies — `ImportError` was silently swallowed on every invocation. The post-processor had been a no-op since extraction in #537. Fix has three parts: (a) `python-docx>=1.1.0` added to runtime dependencies; (b) imports hoisted to module top so a future missing-dep regression fails loudly at orchestrator import time, not silently per-call (fail-closed pattern per `feedback_safety_not_test_convenient`); (c) the in-function except narrowed to `(KeyError, AttributeError, ValueError, OSError, OpcError)` with `pipeline.jsonl` event `cover_letter_spacing_failed` on the exception path — preserves the "cosmetic must not block prep" intent without catching `ImportError`. Bookmark-stripping logic removed entirely from `_add_cover_letter_spacing` (was dead code — `config/strip-bookmarks.lua` already eliminates `<w:bookmarkStart>` emission at pandoc time, verified zero `bookmarkStart` elements in production cover-letter docx output). Test surface: 5 new tests in `tests/test_prep_docx_postprocess.py` — `test_spacing_applied_to_body_paragraphs` (the regression assertion: `space_after >= Pt(12)` on every body paragraph after post-process), `test_heading_and_contact_paragraphs_left_untouched`, `test_date_paragraph_gets_space_before`, `test_empty_paragraphs_not_modified`, `test_missing_file_logs_event_does_not_raise`. Module-top imports also enforce a clean-venv invariant: the test file fails at collection in any venv that doesn't have `python-docx` installed, closing the silent-no-op failure mode against recurrence. Live-verified locally against a saved production cover letter: all body paragraphs picked up `w:after="240"` (240 twips = 12pt) direct formatting in the raw XML; heading + contact-info paragraphs untouched. **No `migration-required`** — runtime-dep + code + role-prompt + test changes only; no schema, config, cron, or mount changes. Container image rebuild required to pick up the new `python-docx` dependency.

- **#678 fix(company_discoverer): raise `max_tokens` to 16384 + emit `openrouter_truncated` on both success and failure paths.** Pre-#678 `config/roles/company_discoverer.md` carried no `max_tokens` frontmatter and inherited the wrapper's `DEFAULT_MAX_TOKENS=4096`. Against Perplexity `sonar-reasoning-pro` (a reasoning model that burns output tokens on reasoning before content), the cap was insufficient: post-onboarding `company_discoverer` runs on a fresh stack reliably hit `finish_reason="length"` with `content=null`, surfaced in `pipeline.jsonl` as `discovery_failed reason=openrouter_error message="Content not a string: NoneType; finish_reason=length"`. Same root cause and same fix shape as #639 (`fit_analyst`) and #666 (`interview_prep`). Two coordinated changes plus a wrapper-level enhancement. (1) **`config/roles/company_discoverer.md` gains `max_tokens: 16384`** — 4× headroom for reasoning + the structured-markdown output the role emits; well within sonar-reasoning-pro's 200K context limit. (2) **`OpenRouterError` gains a structured `finish_reason: str | None = None` attribute** populated in `_parse_response` when the null-content path raises. Pre-#678, callers detecting a budget-exhausted truncation from the failure path had to grep `str(e)` for `finish_reason=length` — brittle to message-format drift. Callers can now branch on `e.finish_reason == "length"` and tests can assert on the structured attribute. (3) **`findajob.discoverer.runner.run` emits `openrouter_truncated` on both paths** — success (when `result.finish_reason == "length"`, placed BEFORE `parse_markdown` so a partial-truncation that also fails parsing still fires the diagnostic) and failure (when `e.finish_reason == "length"` in the `except OpenRouterError` block, placed BEFORE the existing `discovery_failed` log so both events fire — they describe different facts and neither replaces the other). Mirrors the `run_role`-level emission #666 added for roles that route through `findajob.llm.role_runner`; the discoverer calls `complete()` directly so this is its parallel. Test surface: 1 wrapper-level test in `tests/test_llm_openrouter.py` (`test_openrouter_error_carries_finish_reason_on_null_content` — drives the actual null-content path through `_parse_response` and asserts `e.finish_reason == "length"`, closing the prior gap of zero coverage on the null-content error path) plus 3 caller-level tests in `tests/discoverer/test_runner.py` (success-path `length` fires, success-path `stop` does not fire, and an HTTP-boundary regression that drives a `content=null + finish_reason="length"` response through `urlopen` and asserts both `openrouter_truncated` and `discovery_failed` fire in that order). Mutation-tested the negative guard to confirm it is load-bearing. The `openrouter_truncated` event payload (`role`, `completion_tokens`, `content_chars`) matches the shape `run_role` already emits, so `pipeline.jsonl` greps work across both call paths. No `migration-required` — role-frontmatter edit, error-class enhancement, and observability addition; no schema/cron/env changes.

- **#690 fix(gmail-config): `/config/gmail/save` auto-runs the IMAP test when credentials change.** Saving the Gmail config page previously validated the app-password's 16-char alphanumeric shape only — any matching string was accepted, and the operator had to click the separate "Test connection" button to verify the credential actually worked. Save-and-walk-away left Gmail integration silently inactive until the next visit. The onboarding gate at `/onboarding/gmail-config/{session_id}/finish` was already protected by its `state.last_login_at` check; the gap was scoped to the post-onboarding edit path (rotated app password, address change, etc.). Fix: `save_gmail_config` captures the prior `gmail_imap.load_config()` before persisting and, when the address-or-password pair differs from it (or no prior config exists), delegates to a new `_run_imap_test(cfg)` helper extracted from `test_gmail_config` — same IMAP round-trip, same `gmail_state.json` writes, same status mapping (`authorized` / `login_failed` / `connection_error`). Re-saves that only touch `sender_allowlist` skip the IMAP call entirely (no network round-trip on cosmetic edits). Failure UX upgraded: `_card.html` renders an inline recovery hint adjacent to the pill — `login_failed` shows "App password rejected. Generate a new one at myaccount.google.com/apppasswords and save again." with the existing link; `connection_error` shows "Couldn't reach Gmail. Check your network and try again." Hints render on BOTH the save-auto-test path and the explicit `/test` button path (single template). The standalone "Test connection" button stays as a re-test affordance. Test surface: 5 new tests in `tests/test_web_gmail_config.py` (auto-test on new creds, skip on unchanged creds, run on rotated password, inline hint on auth-failure, inline hint on connection-error) plus an inline-hint extension to the existing `/test` AUTH_FAILED test; mutation test confirmed the unchanged-creds guard is load-bearing. No `migration-required` — web-route + template change only, no schema/config/cron impact.

## [0.27.1] — 2026-05-18

### Added

- **#614 feat(settings): `/settings/connections/` — maintenance UI for `data/connections.csv`.** Third occupant of the `/settings/` namespace (joining `/settings/reject-reasons/` and `/settings/active-sources/`); the deferred second half of #571. The page surfaces last-imported timestamp (PT absolute + humanized relative — "3 weeks ago"), row count (via `csv.reader` to handle quoted multi-line fields), refresh/replace upload (atomic `os.replace` via same-dir tempfile), and a destructive Remove affordance gated by a confirm zone that mirrors the #700 regenerate-confirm pattern (GET `/remove/confirm` swaps into `#remove-zone`, POST `/remove` deletes, GET `/remove/cancel` restores the initial button). New shared module `findajob.web.connections_upload` factors out `REQUIRED_COLUMNS`, `MAX_BYTES`, `validate_connections_csv()`, `atomic_write_connections()`, and `count_connections_rows()`; the onboarding gate at `/onboarding/connections/` (#571) refactored to consume the same validator so the two upload paths can't drift on what counts as a valid header / size / encoding. The 28-line LinkedIn-export instructional `<details>` block factored into `templates/settings/_linkedin_export_explainer.html` and `{% include %}`'d from both onboarding and settings pages — same anti-drift rationale, applied to user-facing copy. Sentinel `.onboarding-complete` is explicitly NOT touched by any settings handler (regression guard test included); the sentinel is one-shot at first-run completion only, and silently re-marking from a settings click would let a stuck-mid-onboarding stack escape the onboarding guard. Test surface: 10 new tests in `tests/test_settings_connections.py` (empty state, present state w/ row count + timestamp, refresh atomic replace, validation-error preserves existing file, UTF-8 BOM parity, confirm zone, cancel restoration, delete + empty render, idempotent delete, sentinel-untouched invariant); the 7 onboarding tests stay green against the refactor. No `migration-required` — web-only, no schema or config changes. Closes #614.

### Changed

- **#709 refactor(actions): action helpers defer filesystem ops past DB commit for atomicity.** Action helpers in `findajob.actions` (`handle_rejection`, `handle_not_selected`, `handle_waitlist`, `handle_reactivate`, `un_reject_job`, `un_not_selected_job`, `un_withdraw_job`) previously ran filesystem mutations (folder moves into `_rejected/`/`_waitlisted/`, `NOT_SELECTED_*.txt` marker create/delete) BEFORE their commit decision. `conn.rollback()` reverted DB writes but left filesystem mutations on disk — DB and disk could disagree. Replaces the older `commit=False` kwarg from #707 with a unified `deferred_fs: list[Callable] | None = None` kwarg that controls both transaction ownership AND filesystem-op deferral: when `None` the helper commits and runs fs ops inline; when a list, fs ops are appended as zero-arg closures and deferred to the caller after their `conn.commit()`. `reattribute_from_archive` (the original failure-mode site) now drives one `db.commit()` across both helpers followed by a single deferred-fs loop — failure before commit leaves both DB and disk fully un-mutated. Failure-mode direction flips and is strictly better: today's fs-then-DB broke correctness (folder in `_rejected/` but `stage='scored'` re-surfaces the row); new DB-then-fs leaves only a cosmetic disk artifact (`stage='rejected'` authoritative, folder cosmetic-stranded in `companies/`). Rollback tests across `tests/test_actions.py` and `tests/test_board_actions.py` grow filesystem-state assertions; new 2-marker regression test (`test_un_not_selected_job_multiple_markers_each_closure_binds_its_own_path`) locks in eager closure capture for `un_not_selected_job`'s `glob.glob` loop, defeating the lazy-binding bug a single-marker test cannot catch. Out of scope (filed as #726 follow-up): `un_apply_job` + `reactivate_from_ingest` have the same shape but aren't in #709's AC#2. **No `migration-required`** — pure refactor, no schema/config/cron/mount changes.

### Fixed

- **#723 fix(db): `_rebuild_table_with_indexes` tolerates drift columns in the legacy schema.** When the source schema carries columns the head schema no longer defines, the helper's `INSERT INTO {new} ({legacy_cols}) SELECT {legacy_cols} FROM {legacy_alias}` raises `no such column` mid-flight. Because the helper ran outside the per-migration transaction wrapper, the rename was already committed: the legacy table stayed under the alias and the new table stayed empty until the next data-producing run repopulated it from scratch, severing every prior `audit_log` job_id link. Fix: (1) intersect `legacy_cols` with the head schema's columns (`PRAGMA table_info` of the freshly-created new table) and only copy the overlap — drift columns are dropped silently on the rebuild; (2) add a row-count invariant that raises if `new != legacy` before the legacy `DROP`, so any future partial-copy failure (CHECK violation on a single row, etc.) fails loud instead of silently truncating; (3) wrap the whole rebuild in explicit BEGIN/COMMIT/ROLLBACK so any failure restores the pre-rebuild state. Switched CREATE TABLE from `executescript` to `execute` because `executescript` implicit-commits any open transaction first. New regression test `test_rebuild_tolerates_drift_columns_absent_from_head_schema` exercises a legacy `jobs` carrying pre-M5 drift columns and asserts rebuild succeeds, drift columns dropped, row count preserved, indexes intact, no legacy residue. Stacks with a residual `_jobs_pre_briefing_ready` alias need an out-of-band recovery (stash net-new fingerprints not in legacy → drop broken jobs → rebuild via the fixed logic → merge net-new back → delete orphan `audit_log`); no `migration-required` for the code change itself.

## [0.27.0] — 2026-05-17

### Migration required
- **#277 New `view_prefs` table (migration 0005).** `src/findajob/migrations/0005_view_prefs.sql` creates the per-tab persistence table that drives the new Columns dropdown + filter-state persistence on every board tab. Schema: `tab TEXT PRIMARY KEY CHECK (tab IN (…seven tab ids…))`, `query_string TEXT NOT NULL`, `updated_at TEXT NOT NULL DEFAULT (datetime('now'))`. Bumps `_meta.schema_version` to 5. Idempotent — fresh installs and existing stacks both pick it up on the next `apply_pending` (which `scripts/init_db.py` runs at every container start). No operator action required beyond `docker compose pull && docker compose up -d`. Test fixtures that hand-roll a minimal schema rather than running migrations need `tests.conftest.ensure_view_prefs_table(conn)` after their CREATE statements — added to all 11 board-route tests this PR.

- **#691 jobs.stage CHECK constraint gains `briefing_ready`.** New `findajob.db.migrate._add_briefing_ready_stage_if_needed()` runs on every `apply_pending` and rebuilds the `jobs` table via the rename-create-copy-drop pattern when the live CHECK lacks `'briefing_ready'`. Idempotent — short-circuits when already present. Fresh installs pick up the constraint directly from the (edited) `0001_initial.sql`; existing stacks at `_meta.schema_version=1` absorb it on their next entrypoint run with no schema_version bump and no operator action.
- **#691 background_tasks.kind CHECK constraint gains `prep_phase_b`.** New `findajob.db.migrate._add_prep_phase_b_kind_if_needed()` runs on every `apply_pending` and rebuilds `background_tasks` when the live CHECK lacks `'prep_phase_b'`. Same idempotent rename-create-copy-drop shape; reads the canonical CREATE TABLE from the (edited) `0002_background_tasks.sql`. The new `kind` value lets the watchdog distinguish Phase B subprocess crashes from legacy `kind='prep'` runs and reset stage to `briefing_ready` (preserving the briefing folder) instead of `scored`.
- **#691 rebuild helper preserves indexes (Session 1 fix).** Session 1's `_add_briefing_ready_stage_if_needed()` dropped the five named `jobs` indexes (`idx_jobs_{fingerprint,loose_fingerprint,stage,apply_flag,updated}`) on the rebuild path because `ALTER TABLE ... RENAME` re-attaches indexes to the renamed shell and `DROP TABLE` removes them with it; the new `CREATE TABLE` only re-created the table, not the indexes. Existing stacks at `_meta.schema_version=1` would have silently lost dashboard-query indexes on first boot after the Session 1 PR landed. Fix: extract `_rebuild_table_with_indexes(conn, *, table, migration_filename, legacy_alias)` that re-executes every `CREATE INDEX` for the table from the source migration file after the new `CREATE TABLE`; both `_add_briefing_ready_stage_if_needed` and the new `_add_prep_phase_b_kind_if_needed` route through it. New regression test `test_briefing_ready_rebuild_preserves_jobs_indexes` exercises the legacy → rebuild path and asserts indexes survive — surfaced via direct `sqlite_master` inspection that the test setup snapshots before and after.

### Added
- **#277 feat(web): per-tab Columns dropdown + persisted filter/sort/cols state.** Two layers on top of the #273 filter framework. (1) **Columns ▾ dropdown** in `_filters.html` — Alpine-driven popover (`x-data="{ open: false }"`, parity with the existing enum/date popovers in `_table_header.html`) listing every `ColumnSpec` for the active tab with a checkbox; Apply commits the checked names into a hidden `cols` input that `filters.js` triggers HTMX `change` on, fetching `/rows` with the new `?cols=` and `hx-push-url`-ing the URL. (2) **Per-tab persistence** via new module `findajob.web.view_prefs` + SQLite table `view_prefs` (migration 0005). Cascade: URL `?cols=` + filter params > persisted view_prefs row > `ColumnSpec.default_visible`. Two route-layer helpers in `findajob.web.routes.board` thread the cascade through all 14 board GET handlers (7 page + 7 /rows): `_maybe_redirect_to_persisted(...)` issues a 303 to `?{persisted_qs}` on cold loads (URL with no allowlisted filter state but a persisted row exists); `_persist_view(...)` auto-saves the serialized parsed filters on every page + /rows GET. Persistence allowlist is built from `ParsedFilters` post-parse — `?density=` and other unrelated params (banner-dismissals, archive pagination `offset`) are excluded by construction, never leak into persistence. Explicit clear: `POST /board/{tab}/reset-view` (Reset-to-defaults link in `_filters.html`, 303 back to the bare tab URL). Density is deliberately out of scope for #277 — it remains URL-param-only as before. Test surface: 25 unit tests for `view_prefs` (serialize / load / save / reset / allowlist), 4 migration tests (table shape, CHECK constraint, idempotent replay, schema_version bump), 14 integration tests in `test_web_view_prefs_cascade.py` (auto-save, cold-load redirect, URL-overrides-persisted, reset roundtrip, hyphenated URL tab name → underscore storage tab). All 12 existing board-route test fixtures updated to call the new `ensure_view_prefs_table()` helper (or rely on `init_db.py` migrations if they already do). CLAUDE.md filter-framework section updated with the cascade + storage path. Closes #277.

- **#691 feat(web): rewire `/prep` to `--phase=a` — gate is now reachable from the dashboard (Session 3 fix).** Sessions 1+2 left `POST /board/jobs/{fp}/prep` on the legacy default (`--phase=all`), which meant Phase B ran immediately after Phase A inside the same subprocess and the operator never saw the briefing-first gate. The infrastructure shipped in Sessions 1+2 was unreachable from the operator UI. Fix: `_launch_prep_subprocess(db, job, extra_args=("--phase=a",))` in the `/prep` handler. Now the dashboard's "Flag for Prep" lands at `briefing_ready`, the operator decides via `/materials/{fp}/`, and `POST /materials/{fp}/continue-prep` runs Phase B. `scripts/prep_application.py` keeps `--phase=all` as its CLI default so cron jobs and manual invocations from `docker exec` are unchanged. One-line code change; test surface adds an explicit `assert "--phase=a" in args` to the existing happy-path assertion. Surfaced by `advisor()` during the Session 3 E2E smoke when the smoke job ran through to `materials_drafted` without ever stopping at the gate. CLAUDE.md "Flag for Prep" table row and stage-lifecycle prose updated to match.

- **#691 feat(web): briefing-first-gate route + materials phase-awareness + watchdog (Session 2 of 3).** The user-visible half of the gate: Session 1's dormant `briefing_ready` state now drives a real operator decision flow. (1) **New route `POST /board/jobs/{fp}/continue-prep`** in `findajob.web.routes.board_actions` promotes a `briefing_ready` row to `prep_in_progress` and spawns `scripts/prep_application.py --phase=b`. Gates mirror `/prep` exactly: 404 / idempotent on `prep_in_progress`+`materials_drafted` / 409 on other stages / 402 spend ceiling / 429 queue cap. Subprocess registers a `background_tasks` row with `kind='prep_phase_b'` (distinct from `kind='prep'`) so the watchdog routes Phase B failures to a different reset target. Same 3-job concurrency cap shared with `/prep` and `/reactivate-and-prep`. New log event `web_continue_prep_dispatched`. (2) **`/materials/{fp}/` is phase-aware** — when `stage='briefing_ready'`, the folder view renders a prominent decision panel above the materials: a teal "Continue prep" button + a "Reject…" affordance that surfaces the standard `reject_reasons` dropdown. Both forms post to new materials-flow wrappers (`POST /materials/{fp}/continue-prep`, `POST /materials/{fp}/reject`) that 303-redirect back to `/materials/` — the dashboard-flow `/board/jobs/{fp}/continue-prep` returns an HTMX-shaped `<tr>` and `/board/jobs/{fp}/reject` returns `HTMLResponse("")`, both of which would land a plain-form POST on a broken page (bare `<tr>` or blank). The wrappers apply identical gates and call the identical helpers — they're a page-shape adapter, not a logic fork. The dashboard `_status_cell.html` gains a teal **📋 Briefing** link (to `/materials/{fp}/`) so operators can spot briefing-ready rows on the board and one-click into the gate. Surfaced by advisor at the Session 2 pre-PR checkpoint; the original implementation pointed the forms at the dashboard-flow routes and would have shipped a broken UX. `handle_rejection` writes `feedback_log` exactly as it would from any board tab — the gate path is a different transition *source*, semantics are identical, scorer learns from the decision. The `stage_class` map gains a teal entry for `briefing_ready` so the badge is visually distinct from `prep_in_progress`. (3) **Visibility constants updated** — `briefing_ready` added to `_DASHBOARD_BASE_WHERE` (so the row stays on the dashboard during the gate period) and `FOLDER_STAGES` (so the folder-link affordance renders). (4) **Watchdog**: new `reap_prep_phase_b()` (60min `KIND_TIMEOUT_MINUTES['prep_phase_b']`) routes stuck Phase B subprocesses to `reset_prep_to_briefing_ready` (preserves `prep_folder_path` + briefing folder so retry doesn't re-pay Phase A); new `reap_briefing_ready_stale()` resets `briefing_ready` jobs older than 48h to `scored` *without* nulling `prep_folder_path`, so a re-flag resurfaces the existing briefing. New action helpers: `findajob.actions.reset_prep_to_briefing_ready()` and `reset_briefing_ready_to_scored()`. `main()` emits per-kind counts (`prep_phase_b_failed`, `briefing_ready_stale_reset`) in the `watchdog_run` event so daily-health log scrubs can spot a runaway Phase B or operator-decision backlog. Test surface: 12 new contract tests for `/continue-prep` in `tests/test_board_actions.py::TestContinuePrep`, 8 new tests for the materials phase-awareness in `tests/test_materials_briefing_gate.py`, 8 new watchdog tests in `tests/test_watchdog.py` (Phase B reset preserves folder, doesn't touch `kind='prep'`, audit row distinguishes the transition; 48h reset preserves folder, leaves fresh rows + other stages alone). Session 3 covers E2E smoke on findajob-clean (happy path, decline-from-briefing, 48h watchdog reset, spend-ceiling-at-cap, speculative-row path) + PR review.

- **#691 feat(prep): briefing-first-gate Phase A / Phase B orchestrator split (Session 1 of 3).** `findajob.prep.orchestrator._run_prep` splits into `_run_prep_phase_a` (company_researcher → briefing_writer → fit_analyst → write briefing.md → transition stage to `briefing_ready` with `fit_score`/`probability_score` persisted) and `_run_prep_phase_b` (re-read briefing from disk + scores from DB on entry, run resume_tailor → resume_change_reviewer → cover_letter_writer → recruiter_critic → find_contacts → write checklist → transition stage to `materials_drafted`). `main()` parses a new `--phase=a|b|all` flag (default `all` preserves legacy callers). Phase B failure path is distinct from Phase A: `_handle_phase_b_failure()` resets stage to `briefing_ready` (NOT `scored`) and preserves `prep_folder_path`, so the operator can retry Phase B without re-paying Phase A's ~$0.33 of LLM spend. Phase B failure modes covered: subprocess crash (find_contacts), MIN_BYTES validation failure on resume/cover. Refactor also makes `_run_prep` accept explicit args rather than reading `sys.argv`, enabling 9 new unit tests covering the contract. The `/continue-prep` route, phase-aware materials view, watchdog reap for `prep_phase_b`, and Phase A completion ntfy ride in Session 2; this PR is dormant on user-visible behavior until that follow-up lands.

- **#684 diagnostics: `scripts/read_env_value.py` — safe `data/.env` value reads.** New CLI delegates to `findajob.paths.load_env()` for diagnostic reads of `data/.env`. Motivation: bash sourcing via `set -a; . data/.env; set +a` silently fails on values containing shell metacharacters (a path like `/srv/example/state` gets evaluated as a command and exits "Permission denied" while the surrounding script appears to succeed). The new CLI reads values literally, strips outer quotes uniformly, and exits non-zero on missing file or missing key. `docs/troubleshooting.md` gains a subsection pointing at it. **No `migration-required`** — new script + tests + docs note. Closes #684.

- **#676 feat(onboarding): Step 1 detects API keys present in container env vars (Fly secrets, compose env_file).** Pre-#676 the `/onboarding/` Step 1 form only checked the SQLite credentials-only session row (populated by manual save) for existing keys; it did not consider `os.environ`. On the Fly path that meant an operator who pre-staged `OPENROUTER_API_KEY` / `RAPIDAPI_KEY` as Fly secrets at deploy time had functional keys in the container but Step 1 still presented an empty form, forcing either re-typing the keys into a browser (the workaround during #648 validation) or having the deploy script `exit 1` on empty values. New behavior: `findajob.web.routes.onboarding._env_var_keys()` reads `OPENROUTER_API_KEY` / `RAPIDAPI_KEY` from `os.environ` (covers both delivery paths — Fly secrets surface directly there, and compose's `env_file: ./state/data/.env` materializes data/.env values into the container's environment at startup); when present AND no SQLite credentials row exists yet, the index renders a **detected** branch with masked last-4 tails and a **Use detected keys** button. Clicking the button POSTs to `/onboarding/keys/use-detected`, which re-reads `os.environ` **server-side** (no secrets in hidden form inputs) and reuses the same `validate_*_format` + `verify_*_key` smoke + `set_credentials` chain as the manual form. Failure paths (stale Fly secret, typo'd compose env_file, format-rejected value) re-render the empty form with an error message that names the env var and tells the operator where to look. Override discipline: `/onboarding/?manual=1` suppresses detection for that render only; the existing `POST /onboarding/keys reset=1` path now redirects to `/onboarding/?manual=1` so "Change keys" lands on the empty form rather than the detected UI the operator just opted out of. SQLite still wins when both an existing credentials row and env vars are present — the existing `keys_collected` masked-summary UI takes precedence. **No `migration-required`** — additive route + Jinja conditional, no schema or config changes. Closes #676; unblocks #672 (unaffiliated-tester Fly walkthrough — pre-staged Fly secrets no longer force a re-type).

- **#689 feat(onboarding): strengthen RapidAPI key validation at Step 1 — parity with OpenRouter.** Pre-#689 the `/onboarding/` Step 1 form ran a format check on the RapidAPI key (printable ASCII + no whitespace) but no live smoke check, leaving one specific silent-failure path: a user pastes an OpenRouter key into the RapidAPI field, the format validator accepts it, the bad key is written to `data/.env`, and the pipeline silently fails on the next scheduled triage. Two coordinated changes: (1) **format check tightened** — `validate_rapidapi_format()` now rejects the `sk-or-v1-` prefix (the dominant cross-paste shape) with an error that names the swap and tells the user which field belongs where; no positive RapidAPI prefix is imposed (RapidAPI key format has varied across the platform's history). (2) **new live smoke check** — `findajob.onboarding.rapidapi_smoke.verify_rapidapi_key()` issues one minimal-query GET against the jobs-api14 endpoint using stdlib `urllib` (parity with `openrouter_smoke.py`); the endpoint/host constants are imported from `JobsApi14Adapter` so the probe stays in sync with the upstream the fetcher uses, but the call doesn't instantiate the adapter or read `target_locations.txt` (which doesn't exist at Step 1 yet). The handler at `POST /onboarding/keys` skips the smoke when the field is blank (RapidAPI is optional at Step 1). The 403 failure message disambiguates three causes — invalid key, missing jobs-api14 subscription, and Fly-egress IP region-block (#679 surfaced this third cause as a real Fly tester failure mode) — so testers don't burn time chasing the wrong cause. The "save now, decide later" invariant (Step-1 key survives interview opt-out) is held by absence-of-clear-write paths and called out in a code comment at the only `set_credentials` write site that mutates `tester_rapidapi_key`. Test coverage: format-validator cross-paste rejection, full failure-mode catalog parity for the smoke module, route integration tests for the OpenRouter-in-RapidAPI-field path, the smoke-failure-doesn't-write-DB path, and the blank-skips-smoke tripwire. **No `migration-required`** — pure validator + onboarding-route behavior change. Closes #689; unblocks #672 (unaffiliated-tester Fly walkthrough).

- **#674 audit(api-keys): restructure for unaffiliated user + Step 1 error hints.** Restructures `docs/getting-started/api-keys.md` per a "separate the layers" decision — the doc teaches RapidAPI-the-platform (account, subscriptions, shared-account-key mechanics, free BASIC tiers per feed) and stops short of per-feed sign-up walkthroughs; per-field feed recommendation stays in onboarding's `/onboarding/feed-config/` picker (sourced from the curated `config/rapidapi_feeds.yaml` allowlist). OpenRouter Step 1 error UX hardened: non-401/402/429 failure paths (unrecognized HTTP code, unexpected response shape, non-JSON body, unhandled exception) now append a recovery hint pointing at `https://openrouter.ai/settings/keys` and `https://status.openrouter.ai/`; format-error message hyperlinks `openrouter.ai`; template adds `|urlize` filter so URLs in `keys_error` render clickable. - **#670 docs(cost): `cost.md` — monthly cost expectation for unaffiliated users.** New first-class page at `docs/getting-started/cost.md` answering "what will this cost me per month" before someone signs up. TL;DR scenario table (hosting-only / triage-only / 1 prep/week / 3 preps/week / power user) ranging $4 → $80/mo. Fly hosting section reproduces the published-pricing-grounded $3–5/mo table. LLM spend section grounded in `cost_log` aggregates from a 10-contiguous-day window in early May 2026 (~2,750 calls across 12 operations): per-operation $/call rates (score $0.0015–$0.003, prep ops $0.20–$0.30, full prep run ~$1) plus monthly scenarios. "Where the numbers come from" section discloses n=1 instance methodology + caveats. Linked from root `README.md` Deploy section + `install-fly.md` cost callout. `findajob.web.routes.docs._PAGES` + smoke script extended with the new slug. **No `migration-required`** — docs-only. Closes #670.

- **#669 docs(getting-started): `install-fly.md` — average-user runbook for Fly.io deploy.** Promotes the Fly install path from operator-only documentation (`docs/operations/fly-deploy.md`) to a first-time-deployer-shaped runbook living alongside `install-docker.md`. Per-row affordances: un-not-selected (restores prior stage from `audit_log`), inline reason change, notes editing (consumes F7's `_notes_cell.html`). Adds `un_not_selected_job()` helper. (#698)**

- **#697 feat(rejected-tab): per-row affordances — Un-reject confirm modal, inline reject-reason change dropdown, and 5 new columns.** Rejected tab gains per-row Un-reject button with a confirm modal warning about `feedback_log` deletion (confirm → existing `POST /board/jobs/{fp}/un-reject`; cancel → `GET /un-reject/cell` restores the button). Inline reject-reason change dropdown for `stage='rejected'` rows (no dropdown for `not_selected` — company rejections aren't operator-edited); `POST /change-reject-reason` updates `jobs.reject_reason` in place, writes `audit_log`, and returns the re-rendered cell. Five new columns added to REJECTED_COLUMNS: `relevance_score`, `location`, `remote_status` (default visible), `ai_notes`, `user_notes` (default hidden); `_rejected_query()` SELECT widened accordingly. Establishes reusable `_confirm_modal.html` partial (F6 / Archive parity will reuse next session). No schema migration — code-only change. Closes #697.

### Fixed

- **#668 docs(cleanup): `scripts/{prep_application,find_contacts}.py` flagged as entry-point shims.** Tracked docs (`docs/operations/README.md`, `docs/architecture/file-map.md`) were treating these two scripts as the implementation, when in fact they have been 45-line and 11-line entry-point shims since the M3 extraction. Manual-run commands still work because the shim is the intended user-facing entry, but the "where the logic lives" framing was misleading anyone reading the code. Operations README: shim headings + implementation pointer + `Run by:` clarified with explicit `scripts/` paths. file-map: shim entries tagged + implementation modules under `src/findajob/` added. `docs/getting-started/api-keys.md` needed no edit — the stale CLAUDE.md "Pipeline Context Table" reference was already removed by the #674 api-keys audit (commit 28c2653). **No `migration-required`** — docs-only. Closes #668.

- **#651 chore(cleanup): retired-symbol drift sweep — `poll_flags`, `jobsync rclone` references.** Two known stale `poll_flags` references updated to reference `scripts/watchdog.py` (which superseded `poll_flags.py` in PR #61 2026-04-22): `src/findajob/actions.py:5` docstring and the `CLAUDE.local.md` scheduler-table row. A third known reference in issue #650's body was deleted rather than substituted, because the bullet sat in a "lower-value, defer" skip-list and the substitution would have introduced an intra-body contradiction with watchdog's existing entry in the high-value triggers table. A fourth surfaced by sweep at `src/findajob/web/routes/board_actions.py:47` ("Mirrors scripts/poll_flags.py's cap" — sentence stripped from the `MAX_CONCURRENT_PREPS` docstring; the cap exists for its own stated reason now). Two `jobsync rclone` references deleted (CLAUDE.local.md scheduler-table row, #650 body bullet) — `jobsync` and `rclone` have been absent from `ops/scheduled-jobs.yaml` and the Dockerfile since the rclone removal in #125. Test fixture `test_inject_preserves_other_env_keys` updated to use `OPERATOR_CUSTOM_VAR` (an arbitrary operator-set var) instead of `GOOGLE_API_KEY` (retired in v0.19.0 #455) as the preservation-target example, removing a stale reference to a retired managed key. Sweep verified `sync_sheet` and `gmail_api` are fully clean (zero matches across `src/`, `scripts/`, `tests/`, `docs/`, `ops/`, `config/`). Decision-log entries in `docs/roadmap.md` (rclone tabling, aichat-ng build strategy, poll_flags retirement note) and the legacy-log-file row in `docs/maintainers/data-ownership.md` left in place — decision logs are intentionally chronological accumulation, and the data-ownership row's backup-classification ("rebuildable, safe to drop") remains accurate regardless of which named jobs are still live. **No `migration-required`** — docs + test fixture only. Closes #651.

- **0004_notes_history.sql** — new `notes_history` table for blur-time edit history of `jobs.user_notes`. ## [0.26.0] — 2026-05-16

### Added
- **#671 feat(spend-ceiling): configurable monthly LLM spend ceiling with per-call + launch-time gates, settings UI, onboarding step, and dashboard nudge.**
  Adds a configurable monthly cap on LLM spending stored in `config/spend_ceiling.txt`.
  Once the ceiling is reached, new prep runs, interview prep, and speculative ingest are blocked (HTTP 402) until the next calendar month (UTC); triage and scoring are unaffected.
  Per-call gate: `findajob.spend_ceiling.check_call_gate()` called inside `openrouter.complete()` raises `LLMSpendCeilingExceeded` (re-raised by `role_runner.run_role`, translated to `spend_ceiling_exceeded` kind by `interview_runner._translate()`).
  Launch-time gate: `check_launch_gate(conn)` returns a `LaunchGateRefusal` dataclass checked by 5 route handlers (prep, regenerate, interview, speculative ingest, speculative regenerate) before spawning subprocesses.
  Settings page at `/settings/spend-ceiling/` provides a recommendation calculator (applies-per-week × 4.3 weeks × $0.25/prep + $15.00 scoring floor), numeric override, and disable option.
  Dashboard banner at `/board/dashboard` nudges operators to configure a ceiling when `config/spend_ceiling.txt` is absent; dismissible via cookie.
  New onboarding step at `/onboarding/spend-ceiling/{session_id}/` inserted between interview finalize and the feed-config/gmail-config decision.
  Nav chip extended to 3 states: normal (slate) / warn at ≥90% (amber) / crossed at ≥100% (rose); chip title includes ceiling when set.
  `config/spend_ceiling.txt` added to `/config/` editor allowlist for emergency overrides.
  **No schema migration required.** `config/spend_ceiling.txt` is a new optional config file.

### Fixed
- **#679 fix(jobs_api14): distinct `jobsapi_403` log event with response body excerpt + RapidAPI headers.** Pre-#679 the `_call_with_retry` path treated 403 the same as every other non-OK status — `raise_for_status()` raised `HTTPError`, the generic `except requests.RequestException` caught it, and `log_event("jobsapi_error", ..., error=str(e))` logged only the URL+status string from `requests.HTTPError`. The actual 403 response body (which carries the RapidAPI failure mode — `"You are not subscribed to this API."`, `"You have exceeded the quota for this API."`, etc.) was discarded before reaching the log. Surfaced during the #648 Fly deploy: 128/128 fetch attempts 403'd with no diagnostic signal beyond "Forbidden for url:". This fix adds a 403-specific branch in `_call_with_retry` that logs `jobsapi_403` carrying `status`, `body_excerpt` (first 500 chars of `response.text`), and four RapidAPI headers (`x-ratelimit-requests-remaining`, `x-ratelimit-requests-limit`, `retry-after`, `x-rapidapi-region`). The generic `jobsapi_error` path is unchanged for non-403 errors. `docs/troubleshooting.md` gains a sentence under "No new jobs appearing on the Dashboard" explaining the `"not subscribed"` body case and pointing operators at <https://rapidapi.com> to subscribe the API on the key's account. `live_test` (onboarding spot-check) is intentionally not modified — its 401/403 path already returns an `auth` bucket; the fetch-time signal is what was missing. **No `migration-required`** — purely additive observability + docs. Closes #679.

## [0.25.1] — 2026-05-15

### Fixed
- **#681 fix(onboarding): honor "none" source-selection by gating the registry default on the `.onboarding-complete` sentinel.** Pre-#681 `findajob.fetchers.adapters.registry._read_active_sources` returned the 7-adapter `_DEFAULT_ACTIVE_SOURCES` list whenever `config/active_sources.txt` was absent — including the state #680 produces when a candidate picks "none — Manual only" in Phase-3g source-selection (which correctly writes nothing). Net result before the fix: a user who explicitly opted out of all automated sources still had every default adapter (jobs-api14, jobs-api14-indeed, jsearch, greenhouse, ashby, lever, gmail) attempting calls every triage cycle. The original options (change default to `[]` + 7-line migration / new "no-sources" sentinel file / thread intent through onboarding state) all carried more weight than the bug warranted. Chosen approach: gate the implicit default on the existing `data/.onboarding-complete` sentinel — no new file, no schema change. Five-cell semantic: (1) sentinel absent + file absent → default (legacy stacks pre-#603 unchanged); (2) sentinel absent + file present → parse file (legacy stacks that touched `/settings/` unchanged); (3) **sentinel present + file absent → `[]`** (the fix — user picked "none"); (4) sentinel present + file header-only → default (`/settings/` "uncheck-everything → revert to default" UX preserved per `_write_active_sources` docstring); (5) sentinel present + file with names → parse file (unchanged). All four callers (`iter_configured_adapters`, `/settings/active-sources/`, `/onboarding/feed-config/`, no `admin/stacks` use) handle the empty-list return cleanly already — audit clean, no caller changes alongside the registry fix. New `_onboarding_complete_path()` helper mirrors `_active_sources_path()` so tests can monkeypatch both. Five-cell unit-test coverage in `test_active_sources_parser.py` (one test per cell) plus a `test_iter_configured_adapters_empty_when_onboarded_none` integration test that drives the real orchestrator-facing caller. **Migration required** — see entry below; affects exactly one historical stack (alice) under the operator's control. Closes #681.
